# **Dadi: A Life of Purpose, Love & Devotion**

# **Dadi: A Life of Purpose, Love & Devotion (1944-2026)**

## **üë§ Who She Was**

Born in Delhi, 1944\. Seventh child in her family. Daughter of a railway mail guard (Senior Mail Guard who raised the flag at the station). A woman who broke barriers, pursued knowledge relentlessly, and dedicated 81 years to service, family, and unwavering faith. She lived in railway bungalows, walked kilometers to school with cloth bags, and grew up in an era without electricity or running water \- yet she never stopped reaching higher.

## **üìö The Scholar & Educator**

* **Education Pioneer**: Fought to continue her education when families didn't prioritize girls' schooling  
* **Government Girls Higher Secondary School, Dariyaganj, Delhi** \- High school  
* **Ramjas College, Morris Nagar, Delhi** \- B.A. Honours in Economics (studying in English, making notes in English, reading writers like Bentham and Malthus)  
* **Delhi School of Economics Library** \- Member, deepening her knowledge  
* **M.A. in Economics** (Meerut University ‚Üí Agra University after universities split)  
* **B.Ed. 1971** \- Became a mathematics teacher  
* **Teaching Career**: Taught Arithmetic, Geometry, and Algebra to 8th grade students. Known for teaching without looking at books \- everything from memory. Students' mothers still remember her fondly.

## **üéñÔ∏è The Warrior Spirit**

* **NCC (National Cadet Corps)**: Three years of service (First, Second, Third year of college)  
* **1962 Indo-China War Response**: Received rifle training, learned to shoulder a rifle and aim  
* **Daily Drill**: One hour of marching, formation exercises with sticks  
* **Philosophy Learned**: "Do and Die" \- a motto she carried throughout life  
* **Sports**: Played throwball/baseball, long jump, led exercise groups with staffs that had bells

## **üåè Life's Journey Across India**

**Delhi** (1944-1967) \- Childhood in Dariba Kalan, Old Delhi, near Red Fort and Chandni Chowk  
 **Jodhpur** (1967-1973) \- Sardarpura, B Road, Shiv Nivas \- where two sons were born  
 **Kota** (1973-1975) \- Shopping Center, Ghumanpura \- where third son was born  
 **Ajmer** (1975-1976) \- Raja Cycle area, near Martingal Bridge  
 **Udaipur** (1976-1981) \- Residency Road, Bhatt Ji Ki Bari, Bhopal Pura  
 **Jaipur** (1981-2025) \- 42 years in the same home, her longest and final residence

## **üí™ The Lifelong Learner**

She never stopped growing:

* **1959**: First Aid certification (St. John Ambulance, Delhi)  
* **1978**: Food Preservation (Udaipur) \- candy, jelly, jam, squashes, syrups  
* **1981**: Cookery & Bakery (Khasa Kothi, Jaipur) \- pizza, cakes, breads  
* **1987**: Cutting & Tailoring (6-month course) \- making clothes for her entire family  
* **1987**: Music (Second Year certification) \- Tabla and Harmonium from Prayag University  
* **2001**: Astrology (from Chennai)  
* Also: Kitchen Gardening Association member, won prizes for her garden

## **üë®‚Äçüë©‚Äçüëß‚Äçüë¶ Her Family & Values**

* **Married**: 1967, to a Union Bank of India officer who rose from Clerk to Manager  
* **Mother of 3 sons**: Raised them without tutors, teaching them herself until 12th grade  
* **Her Core Teaching**:  
  * "Never steal, never lie, never hurt anyone's tongue (heart) \- this is service to God"  
  * "Share everything you eat \- distribution, not hoarding"  
  * "If you find something, don't keep it. Return it or donate it to temple"  
  * "Work hard for what you want. Never take what isn't yours"  
* **Living Example**: When a son wanted to keep a pencil from school, she made him return it immediately  
* **Extended Family**: Took in and supported siblings-in-law, helped with their education, marriages, and jobs without ever complaining

## **üè† The Homemaker**

She believed her home was her temple:

* **Standard of Living**: Studied development of USA, Russia, Japan, England while doing her Economics degree. Applied those principles: "How do I develop my home? How do I raise my standard of living?"  
* **Choice**: Chose family over career \- "If I work, I'd have two jobs. Better to do one job perfectly."  
* **Cleanliness**: Obsessive about hygiene \- even dustbins had to be scrubbed clean. Washed buckets and mugs before every bath.  
* **Daily Routine**: Up early, 2-3 hours of house cleaning and organizing by noon, then spiritual practices

## **üïâÔ∏è Her Spiritual Journey**

* **Childhood Devotion**: At 9-10 years old, wrote 2,500 Gayatri mantras (certificate from 1960 still preserved)  
* **Service to Elders**: Read Krishna Leela and Ramayana to her illiterate grandmother  
* **Daily Practice in Final Years**:  
  * 7:00 AM temple visits for three aartis (Shiv ji, Ram-Krishna-Hanuman, Radha Govind, Ganesh ji)  
  * Writing "Jai Shri Krishna" 888 times daily (4 malas, 2 pages, 222 names per page)  
  * Reading Bhagavad Gita for life guidance  
  * Attending Shiv Puran recitations  
* **The Four Ashrams**: She lived consciously through each stage:  
  * **Bal Ashram (0-25)**: Learning and education  
  * **Grihastha Ashram (25-50)**: Family and responsibilities  
  * **Vanprastha Ashram (50-75)**: Guidance and stepping back  
  * **Sanyas Ashram (75+)**: Devotion and detachment \- "Cut ties slowly, focus on God"

## **üíô Her Essence**

**Favorite Color**: Sky blue \- "Aasmani"  
 **Favorite Animal**: Parrots (kept them at home, fed cows daily bread)  
 **Favorite Food**: All vegetables \- "Each has different qualities, I eat them all"  
 **Health Conscious**:

* Learned from childhood health lectures: "Wash mouth and eyes with water held in cheeks" \- kept her eyes perfect at 81  
* Strong teeth from chewing raw sugarcane (ganna) her whole life  
* After hospitalization (blood sugar dropped to 31), followed doctor's orders religiously: eat every 2 hours

## **üåü Her Philosophy**

From the Bhagavad Gita, she believed:

* **Karma**: "Give happiness, receive happiness. Give sorrow, receive sorrow 10-fold"  
* **Yogini (Rebirth)**: Do good deeds (Satvik karma) ‚Üí get Dev yoni (godly birth). Do average deeds (Rajas karma) ‚Üí get human birth. Do bad deeds (Tamas karma) ‚Üí get lower births  
* **No Enemies**: "Every person is their own friend or enemy. Don't create enemies, create friends"  
* **Let Go of Bad**: "If you see someone's bad qualities, turn away and walk your own path. Don't hold hatred"  
* **Equanimity**: "Don't be too happy or too sad. Treat everything equally and move forward with good things"

## **üíî Final Chapter**

In her final years, she had completed her duties:

* All three sons educated (one to IIT), married, settled  
* Grandchildren thriving  
* She had transitioned fully into Sanyas Ashram  
* "I don't want moksha (liberation) immediately. Do good deeds, enjoy heaven for a while, then come back to serve again"  
* She survived a critical health scare (blood sugar 31\) because "everyone's prayers worked"  
* She lived simply, prayed daily, and found peace in routine and devotion

## **üìñ Her Legacy**

She didn't pursue a PhD or a big career, but she created something greater: three educated sons, a loving family spanning four generations, and a living example of how to walk through life with integrity, devotion, and grace.

Her students remember her. Their mothers still speak of her. Her children embody her values. Her grandchildren recorded her stories. Her great-grandchildren will know her voice.

---

**She didn't just live 81 years. She lived with purpose, raised her family with values, never stopped learning, served everyone without expectation, maintained rigorous discipline in cleanliness and spirituality, and spent her final years in peaceful devotion.**

**From railway bungalows without electricity to modern Jaipur, from partition-era India to the digital age, from a young NCC cadet with a rifle to a grandmother writing "Jai Shri Krishna" 888 times daily \- she witnessed and adapted to everything while never compromising her core values.**

**Rest in eternal peace, Dadi. Your light continues through all of us.** üôè‚ú®

*"‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§•‡§æ \- ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§®‡§æ"*  
 *"My purpose was \- to help my children progress"*

# **Dadi Quotes**

# **In Loving Memory of Dadi**

## **Her Words, Her Wisdom, Her Legacy**

*February 8, 2026*

---

### **On Education & Determination**

**"‡§π‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á"**  
 **"I will study"**

*When the family resisted sending me for higher education, I stood firm. I had to struggle for college education, especially as a girl in the 1950s, but I never gave up.*

---

### **On Family Service**

**"‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç, ‡§ö‡•å‡§•‡•á ‡§™‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡•à, ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å‡•§ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§á‡§ú‡§º ‡§µ‡§∞‡§∂‡§ø‡§™ ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç‡•§"**

**"I have three children, fourth is my husband, fifth is myself. Their work is my work. That work IS worship. These are all God's beings."**

*Serving family is serving God. This was my life's dharma.*

---

### **The Three Commandments (From My Mother)**

**"‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡•§ ‡§ù‡•Ç‡§† ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§¨‡•ã‡§≤‡•ã‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§, ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§≠ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡•§"**

**"Don't steal. Don't lie. Don't hurt anyone with your tongue. This itself is serving God."**

*These three principles guided every decision I made.*

---

### **On Sharing**

**"‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Å‡§ü ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì‡•§"**

**"Whatever you eat, eat by sharing."**

*I taught my children: when grapes came, divide them. Give everyone their share. Even give me some \- I also want to eat\! This way they learned: we must share what we receive.*

---

### **On Honesty**

**"‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§π‡§®‡§§ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡•§ ‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§™‡•á‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∏ ‡§¶‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ì‡•§ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ä‡§Å‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡•§"**

**"Earn by your own hard work. Even if my children took a pencil by mistake, I said: Return it immediately. If you don't, I'll go to school and return it myself."**

*They never brought home anything that belonged to others.*

---

### **On Making Friends, Not Enemies**

**"‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•à, ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§ò‡•É‡§£‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡•§ ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å ‡§™‡•à‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã, ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§ì ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•ã‡•§"**

**"Human being is their own friend, their own enemy. Don't hate anyone. Don't create enemies, make everyone friends."**

---

### **On Handling Negativity**

**"‡§¨‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§à ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•á‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§®‡•á, ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Å‡§π ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§°‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§ï‡§°‡§º ‡§≤‡•ã‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§®‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ì, ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§™‡§ï‡§°‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡•ã, ‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§´‡•á‡§Ç‡§ï ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ï‡§ö‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ü‡•ã‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡•§"**

**"If you see evil in someone, leave it right there. Turn your face and take your own path. Neither be too happy nor be sad. Consider everyone equal. Catch the good things and move forward \- throw the bad things in the garbage basket."**

---

### **On Life's Stages (The Four Ashrams)**

**"‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ \- ‡§¨‡§ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç \- ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç, ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä, ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§º‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Å‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å \- ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á-‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§π‡§∞ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ó‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ, ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§§‡§∞‡§π ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Å \- ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à‡•§"**

**"I passed through each ashram properly: childhood with learning, householder stage with all family duties, and now in sanyas \- gradually detaching from worldly things and engaging in God. Whatever stage I'm in, I should pass through it properly \- this is my purpose."**

---

### **On Karma & Rebirth**

**"‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡•§ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡•§ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç ‡•ß‡•¶ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•á‡§Ç, ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è, ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§∏‡•§"**

**"If you give happiness, you'll receive happiness. If you give comfort, you'll receive comfort. If you give sorrow, you'll receive sorrow. After death, these things return tenfold. Do good deeds, go to good rebirth, keep good thoughts \- that's all."**

---

### **On Service & Debt**

**"‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à \- ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§®‡•Ç‡§Å ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á? ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•Ä, ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡•á ‡§¨‡•á‡§ü‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ã, ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö‡§≤‡•ã, ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ã‡§£ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ä‡§™‡§∞ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§¢‡§º‡•á‡•§"**

**"I was indebted to everyone, which I kept repaying. If virtuous work is happening, why should I become party to sin by refusing? Don't take anyone's service \- even from your own son. Do his work yourself, so his debt doesn't accumulate on you."**

---

### **On Never Stopping Learning**

**"‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ: ‡•ß‡•Ø‡•´‡•Ø ‡§´‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü ‡§è‡§°, ‡•ß‡•Ø‡•≠‡•Æ ‡§´‡•Ç‡§° ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ú‡§º‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§®, ‡•ß‡•Ø‡•Æ‡•ß ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•á‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä, ‡•ß‡•Ø‡•Æ‡•≠ ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ü‡•á‡§≤‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó, ‡•®‡•¶‡•¶‡•ß ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∑, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§ö‡§® ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§°‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó, ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§ú‡§º‡§ø‡§ï‡•§ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§π‡•â‡§¨‡•Ä ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•ã‡•§"**

**"I never stopped learning: First Aid at 19, Food Preservation at 38, Cookery at 41, Tailoring at 47, Astrology at 61\. Keep developing some hobby or other."**

---

### **On Daily Practice**

**"‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú‡§º ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å \- ‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡•§ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡•§ ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å \- ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§® ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à, ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡•§"**

**"Every day I write two pages \- Jai Shri Krishna. Four malas. From this I have received very good peace. I read Gita \- it teaches me how to live life."**

---

### **The Steel Body**

**"‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•à‡§Ç‡§° ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•Ä‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•â‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§à ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã, ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç‡•§ Do and Die \- ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡•§"**

**"They built and gave me a body of steel. Do any amount of work, no illness comes. 'Do and Die' \- this is still running in my mind."**

*From NCC training, 1963\. The spirit of determination never left me.*

---

### **Her Final Philosophy**

**"‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§® ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•Å‡§Ü‡§è‡§Å ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§à‡•§ ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à‡•§"**

**"My life now is proceeding like this. Now all of you people's prayers worked. I'm alive."**

---

**Born: 1942, Delhi | Departed: 2026, Jaipur**  
 **Lived: 84 years of determination, service, and unwavering principles**

*"‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§∏" \- Keep good thoughts, that's all.*

**üôè Om Shanti Shanti Shanti üôè**

# **Dadi First-Hand Summary**

# **Dadi's Life Story \- Summary**

*As told during video call with grandchildren, January 2023*

## **Early Life & Childhood (1940s-1950s)**

I was born in Delhi, the seventh child in my family \- I had four brothers and three sisters. My father worked as a Senior Mail Rail Guard in the railways, and we lived in a large railway bungalow behind the station. Life was different then \- we had no running water or electricity in the early days. We used lamps and lanterns that had to be cleaned every morning with ash and cloth.

For water, we hired a man who carried two aluminum cans (16 liters each) on his shoulders using a wooden pole. We would arrange for four trips daily \- eight cans total. When we needed more water, we children would walk 100 meters to the tap and carry buckets ourselves.

I walked about 1.5 kilometers to the railway school every day, carrying my cloth bag on my shoulder. We got milk at school since it was a railway school, and fees were deducted directly from my father's salary.

## **Health Habits That Last a Lifetime**

A sadhu (holy man) once visited our school and taught us to splash water on our face and eyes \- I still do this today, and at 81, my eyesight is excellent. Doctors are amazed by my eye health.

We ate a lot of sugarcane \- peeling it with a knife and chewing the raw cane. We would buy one "man" (about 40 kg) of sugarcane at a time, sit on the roof, break it at the joints, peel it with our teeth, and extract the juice. Even the dentist who treated me at 80 years old said my teeth are remarkably strong because of this practice. I continued eating sugarcane even after marriage.

## **Education \- A Struggle Worth Fighting For**

When my father retired in 1955, he had no pension \- only provident fund (PF). He had five children's weddings to arrange. I had to struggle to continue my education because girls' education wasn't always encouraged then. But I insisted \- I wanted to study further.

In 1956, at age 16, we moved back to Delhi. We lived at 152 Katra Mashroom, Dariba Kalan, in Old Delhi \- our family home with 22-24 small rooms arranged around a central courtyard. My sister-in-law helped enroll me in Government Girls Higher Secondary School near Rajghat, about 4-5 kilometers from home.

Initially, a bus ran for one month (one rupee for the month\!), but then it stopped. After that, I walked daily \- it took half an hour from Parade Ground through Dariyaganj. I studied there through 8th, 9th, 10th, and 11th.

## **College Years at Ramjas College**

My third brother, who studied at Ramjas College, helped me get admission there. He knew the Head of the Economics Department, N. Agarwal. Ironically, Economics was my weakest subject \- I had only 60% in it, though I had distinction marks in Lower Mathematics and Domestic Science. But they admitted me anyway.

I studied BA Honours in Economics at Ramjas College, Maurice Nagar. I took special buses from Lal Qila to Maurice Nagar every day. I was a member of Delhi School of Economics library and read English writers like Bentham and Malthus. Everything was in English \- lectures, notes, exams.

I completed my MA first year from Meerut University, but when Meerut and Agra Universities separated, I completed my final year from Agra University in 1968, after marriage.

## **NCC Training \- A Soldier's Experience**

I did NCC (National Cadet Corps) for three years during college \- equivalent to the US reserves. We wore uniforms, did marching drills for an hour, and got 10 grams of butter and a roll.

After the 1962 China war, in my third year, they gave us rifle training. I learned to shoulder the rifle and aim properly. We learned "do or die" \- that spirit still runs in my mind. Though I never went on active duty, the training shaped my character.

## **Sports & Activities**

I played throwball, which was like baseball \- you hit the ball with a bat and run touching bases. I was also the group leader and taught others to play with the musical stick (with bells that made jingling sounds). I did long jump too.

I learned tabla and harmonium starting from 1954 and even passed the second year music exam from Allahabad University. After marriage in Jaipur, I continued learning, but stopped when my young brother-in-law (41 years old) passed away \- I thought people would criticize me for playing music during mourning.

## **Marriage & Teaching Career (1967)**

I married in 1967 at age 27 \- late for those times, but because I insisted on completing my education first. My husband worked in Union Bank of India and eventually became a Manager.

Even while pregnant with my first child, I taught mathematics to 8th grade students \- arithmetic, geometry, and algebra \- from July to December 1968\. I taught without even opening textbooks; my mathematics was that strong. I got a certificate saying I taught excellently.

In Jodhpur, I earned 15 rupees salary initially. After completing B.Ed., I got 50 rupees at Lalwani School.

## **Journey Across Rajasthan**

**Jodhpur (1967-1973)**: We lived at Shivniwas, Sardarpur B Road. My first two sons were born here. Bank provided housing since my husband was a manager.

**Kota (1973-1975)**: Lived near Shopping Center, Ghumanpura. My third son was born here. Children attended St. Paul's School.

**Ajmer (1975-1976)**: Very brief stay, about 6 months to a year. Lived near Raja Cycle and Martin Bridge.

**Udaipur (1976-1981)**: Lived at Residency Road, then Bhatt Ji ki Badi for five years. All three boys studied at St. Paul's School here.

**Jaipur (1981-present)**: First lived behind Khasa Kothi near railway station, at Gangaur Hotel area. The landlord wanted us to vacate, so we bought our current house. We moved here when my eldest was in 7th grade, middle son in 3rd, and youngest in 1st. That was 42 years ago \- we've been in this house since 1981\.

## **Courses & Skills \- Never Stop Learning**

I've taken so many courses throughout my life:

* **1954-onwards**: Tabla and Harmonium  
* **1959**: First Aid course in Delhi from St. Ambulance  
* **1978**: Food Preservation in Udaipur (making toffees, jellies, jams, candies, squashes, syrups)  
* **1981**: Cookery & Bakery course in Jaipur at Khasa Kothi (Government of India run, one month course on alternate days \- learned to make pizza, cakes, etc.)  
* **1987**: Cutting & Tailoring course (6 months \- learned to make pajamas, vests, frocks, blouses, salwar kameez, nightsuits, pants, shirts)  
* **Kitchen Gardening Association**: Joined and won several prizes  
* **2001**: Astrology course in Chennai \- studied with my husband  
* **Also taught Food Preservation** for one month at Maharaja School

My certificates are all compiled together by my daughter-in-law Kokila.

## **Philosophy of Life \- The Four Ashrams**

I studied the development of USA, Russia, Japan, and England during my Economics degree. India was a developing country, rich in resources but inhabited by poor people. I thought: how can we develop by properly utilizing natural resources? This stayed in my mind \- how to advance ourselves, how to advance our children.

Life has four ashrams:

1. **Bal Ashram (0-25 years)**: Childhood and learning  
2. **Grihastha Ashram (25-50 years)**: Family life  
3. **Vanprastha Ashram (50-75 years)**: Gradual withdrawal  
4. **Sanyas Ashram (75+ years)**: Spiritual focus

Now at 81, I'm in Sanyas Ashram. I need to gradually detach from worldly things and focus on God. I don't like attending too many social functions or weddings anymore. I prefer solitude to focus on my daily spiritual practices.

## **Daily Spiritual Practice**

Every day I write "Jai Shri Krishna" \- two pages, which equals four malas (rosaries) of 108 names each. I write 222 names per page (6 columns x 37 names). I write in advance so that if something happens (like my recent hospitalization), I'm never behind.

I go to temple every morning at 7 AM for three aartis \- Shiv ji's aarti, Om Jai Jagdish Hare for Ram-Krishna-Laxman-Sita-Hanuman and Radha Govind, and Ganesh ji's aarti. I take prasad and return home.

I read Bhagavad Gita regularly. It teaches me how to live life, how to understand others, about prakriti (nature) and why God created different life forms. I recently attended Shiv Puran discourse from November 24-30 and December 30-January 9\.

## **Values I Taught My Children**

I raised my three sons with strong values my mother taught me:

* **Don't steal** \- even if you find something lying around, give it to the temple, don't keep it  
* **Don't lie**  
* **Don't hurt anyone with your words**  
* **Share everything you eat** \- I taught them to divide things among themselves and always give me a portion too  
* **Work hard and earn honestly**

I never hired tutors for my children. I taught all three myself through 12th grade. They never stole, never lied. If they took even a pencil by mistake, I made them return it.

My mother's teaching: serving family is serving God. My work is worship. These three children, my husband, and I \- serving these five was my life's work.

## **Principles of Living**

I never gossiped. If someone insulted me, my mother taught me: "The insult is not yours if you don't accept it." I would feel hurt, share my pain to lighten it, but not seek revenge. I simply stayed away from people who were negative.

I believe in karma \- what you give, you receive. Give happiness, receive happiness. Give sorrow, receive sorrow. After death, it comes back tenfold. If you steal one rupee, you'll have to repay ten in the next life.

The subtle body (with mind, consciousness, intellect, and all sensory actions) goes with you, not the physical body. According to Gita, good (satvik) actions lead to dev yoni (divine birth), rajasic actions lead to human birth, and tamasic actions lead to lower births.

I don't want moksha (liberation) where you merge with God. I want to keep coming back to serve, to do good deeds.

## **Recent Health Scare**

Recently, my sugar level dropped to 31, and I had to be rushed to the hospital. My grandson Bhavya immediately took me \- if we'd been five minutes late, who knows what would have happened. The doctor said to eat something every two hours. Now I follow this strictly.

Despite this scare, I maintain my routines. I clean everything myself \- even the dustbin must be spotless, scrubbed with soap if needed. I wash every bucket and mug before bathing. No compromises on cleanliness and hygiene.

## **Looking Back with Gratitude**

I was an idealistic person, spiritual even as a young girl. I wrote 2,500 and 5,000 Gayatri Mantras in 9th-11th grade. I still have the paper from 1960 when I sent 2,500 mantras to Mathura Tapobhumi.

I read Krishna Leela and Ramayana to my grandmother (your great-great-grandmother on your father's side) since she couldn't read. She was from Harsoli village near Rewari in UP, and my grandfather was from Rewari. She was an ideal lady with great character and principles.

My focus has always been: raise good children, maintain high standards of living, keep learning, keep serving. I never became a burden on anyone \- I did everything myself so I wouldn't be indebted to anyone, not even my own children.

Today, at 81, my body is still strong \- like steel, I used to say. I built it with all those childhood activities, walking, sports, and good nutrition. Though I've slowed down, I'm still independent, still doing my daily practices, still writing my malas, still going to temple.

This is my life \- lived with determination, faith, service, and constant learning. Never stop growing, never stop serving.

---

*"The enemy and friend are both within you. Make everyone your friend. Don't create enemies. Move forward catching good things, throw bad things in the garbage basket. This is how life should be lived."*

# **Dadi First-Hand**

  * 4 brothers  
  * 3 sisters (2 older, 1 younger than me)

## **Early Childhood (1940s-1950s)**

### **Living Conditions \- Railway Bungalow Era (1951-1955)**

#### **The Railway Bungalow**

* **Location:** Behind the railway station  
* **Type:** Large railway bungalow (government quarters)  
* **Size:** 3-4 rooms  
* **Bathroom/Toilet:** Outside the main house  
* **Veranda:** Yes, had a large veranda  
* **Front area:** Lots of fencing, servant quarters  
* **Reason for housing:** Father was Senior Mail Rail Guard in railways

#### **Servant Quarters**

The railway compound had separate servant quarters where:

* One teacher lived  
* One washerwoman (dhoban) lived  
* They helped us with daily work

#### **Earlier Living Conditions (Before 1953-54)**

**Pre-Electricity Era:**

* **No electricity** in the quarter initially  
* **Lighting:** Used lamps and lanterns  
* **Daily maintenance routine:**  
  * Every morning, or in the evening, family members would clean the lamp chimneys  
  * Cleaned with ash  
  * Wiped with cloth  
  * Prepared them for evening/night use  
* **When lamps burned:** Evening and night time

**Kitchen Arrangements:**

* No separate kitchen room  
* No modern stove/latrine/bathroom facilities  
* Had storage rooms  
* **Cooking setup:**  
  * One small room used for cooking  
  * Stone shelf (‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§§‡§æ‡§®) built into the wall  
  * Items stored on the shelf  
  * Below: Either angithi (coal stove) or chulha (traditional clay stove)  
  * Food cooked on these traditional stoves

**The Water Challenge (1950s):**

Since there was no running water or tap in the house:

1. **The Water Carrier System:**

   * Hired a man specifically for water delivery  
   * He carried a wooden pole (‡§≤‡§ï‡§°‡§º‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•à‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä) on his shoulders  
   * Thick iron wire/rod suspended from the pole  
   * The wire had hooks (‡§ï‡•Å‡§Ç‡§°‡§æ) at the ends  
2. **Water Containers:**

   * Used cut ghee/oil canisters (tin containers)  
   * Cut in half  
   * Wooden handle attached through the middle  
   * The handle would hook onto the curved hooks on the pole  
3. **Capacity & Delivery:**

   * **Each canister:** 16 liters  
   * **Per trip:** 2 canisters \= 32 liters total  
   * **Our daily order:** 4 trips \= 8 canisters  
   * **Total daily water:** Approximately 128 liters (32 liters √ó 4 trips)  
4. **Additional Water Needs:**

   * We maintained cleanliness standards  
   * Had many plants and a lawn with hedges all around  
   * Brothers took care of the garden  
   * **When more water needed:**  
     * We children would go to the public tap ourselves  
     * The tap was about 100 meters away  
     * We'd fill buckets and carry them back  
     * This way we managed our daily needs

**Bathing Arrangements:**

* Curtain hung in the veranda area  
* Iron grill (‡§ú‡§æ‡§´‡§∞‡•Ä) already installed  
* Created a screened area for privacy  
* Had a drain (‡§®‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä) so water would flow out  
* Like a small enclosure \- water wouldn't spill outside  
* We would bathe there with buckets

### **The Big Change (1954-1955)**

**Timeline of Major Life Changes:**

* **1951-1953:** Living in railway bungalow, these childhood memories  
* **1954:** Second elder brother's wedding (I remember this one clearly)  
* **1955:** Father retired from railway service  
* **1956:** Moved back to Delhi for education

---

## **Elementary Education**

### **Railway School Years (1946-1955)**

#### **Starting Education**

* **School Start:** Around 1946-1947 (when I was approximately 6-7 years old)  
* **Clear memories begin:** From age 9-10 (around 1950\)  
* **School Type:** Railway School (for children of railway employees)  
* **Distance:** About 1.5 kilometers from home  
* **Travel:** Walked on foot daily

#### **School Bag & Supplies**

* **Type:** Cloth bag, like a cloth sack (‡§•‡•à‡§≤‡•Ä)  
* Description: "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§•‡•à‡§≤‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•à‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¨‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ"  
* Filled with our school materials  
* Carried on shoulder while walking to school

#### **School Benefits (Railway School Privileges)**

Since it was a railway school:

* **Free milk** provided at school  
* **Fee structure:** Very nominal  
* **Fee payment method:**  
  * Deducted for 2 months at a time from father's salary  
  * All expenses deducted first  
  * Father received remaining salary after all deductions

#### **Teachers & Address**

* Called **"Master Sahab"** (‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§¨)  
* Also addressed as **"Bhaiya Ji"** (‡§≠‡•à‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä)  
* They taught us well with proper lectures

### **Health & Hygiene Education**

#### **The Sadhu's Visit \- A Lesson That Lasted a Lifetime**

**The Event:**

* Sometimes school would invite a sadhu/saint for special lectures  
* They would come and teach about health maintenance  
* One particular lesson I still remember and practice

**The Eye Care Method:**

* Fill mouth with water  
* Splash the water on face and eyes (‡§™‡•Å‡§ö ‡§™‡•Å‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á)  
* Rinse and splash repeatedly  
* **Result:** My eyesight is still excellent at 81  
* **Doctor's confirmation:** The surgeon who examined me said my nerves are in very good condition  
* I still show my eyes regularly at this age

**Impact:**

* I continue this practice every single day  
* At 81 years, my eyes are perfectly fine  
* This childhood teaching became a lifelong habit

#### **Dental Health \- The Sugarcane Secret**

**The Practice:**

* We ate a lot of sugarcane (‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ)  
* Method:  
  * Peel the sugarcane  
  * Chew it with teeth to extract the juice (‡§ó‡§Ç‡§°‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡•Ç‡§∏‡§æ)  
* **Started in childhood, continued after marriage**

**Buying in Bulk:**

* Would buy sugarcane by the "man" (‡§Æ‡§® \- unit of weight, approximately 40 kg)  
* One entire "man" at a time  
* Sit on the roof terrace (‡§õ‡§§)  
* Break it at the joints using a knife  
* Peel with mouth/teeth  
* Chew the inner part (‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä)

**Details of the Process:**

* The sugarcane has joints/nodes (‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ç‡§†)  
* Break it at these joints  
* Can peel it using a knife or teeth  
* Between the two joints, peel off the outer covering  
* Use mouth to do this  
* Then chew the sugarcane to get the sweet juice  
* Discard the fibrous remains

**Medical Confirmation:**

* At 80-81 years old, during recent dental treatment  
* **Doctor's comment:** "Your teeth are very strong"  
* Direct result of eating sugarcane throughout life  
* This practice continued regularly even after marriage

### **Other School Activities**

#### **Physical Education**

* Did long jump (played ‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§¶) up to 8th standard  
* Played throwball in 9th, 10th, and 11th  
* Played Kho-Kho in middle school  
* Played Kabaddi  
* Played Gilli Danda

**Result:** Built a solid body \- "Built a body of steel"

---

## **Life in Delhi & Higher Education**

### **The Move to Delhi (1956)**

#### **Family Home in Old Delhi**

* **Full Address:** 152 Katra Mashroom (K-A-T-R-A M-A-S-H-R-O-O-M), Dariba Kalan (D-A-R-I-B-A K-A-L-A-N), Delhi  
* **Area:** Old Delhi (not New Delhi)  
* **Landmarks nearby:**  
  * Dariba Kalan Road  
  * Red Fort (Lal Qila) \- very close to our house  
  * Chandni Chowk \- nearby  
  * Splendid Road \- nearby  
  * Bhagirathi Palace/Market \- close by  
  * Daau Ji's temple on Splendid Road

#### **The Family House**

* **Ownership:** Our own house (not rented)  
* **Size:** 22-24 rooms (very large ancestral home)  
* **Room size:** Small rooms  
* **Layout:** Traditional courtyard house  
  * Central courtyard (‡§ö‡•å‡§ï) in the middle  
  * Rooms arranged all around the courtyard on all four sides  
* **Purchase:** My grandfather bought this house **86 years before 1956** (so around 1870\!)  
* **Family continuity:**  
  * After grandfather, my father inherited it  
  * Father retired and came here in 1956  
  * We lived here from 1956 until my marriage in 1967  
  * Our family had this house for generations

### **The Struggle for Higher Education (1956-1964)**

#### **Why It Was a Struggle**

**Family Financial Situation After Father's Retirement (1955):**

* Father retired from railway  
* **No pension** \- only Provident Fund (PF) received as lump sum  
* **Major responsibilities:**  
  * Had to arrange 5 weddings  
  * Including my wedding  
  * Brothers' and sisters' weddings

**Societal Pressure:**

* Girls' education wasn't always encouraged in those days  
* Family was not ready to let me continue studying  
* There was resistance to sending me for higher education

**My Determination:**

* **I said:** "‡§π‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á" (I will study)  
* I insisted on continuing my education  
* Had to struggle for this, especially for college education  
* But I stood firm

**Father's Support:**

* Great-Great-Nanaji (my father, your Papa's great-grandfather)  
* Eventually gave his permission  
* Allowed me to pursue higher studies  
* This was progressive thinking for that era

#### **Two Weddings During My Education**

To manage finances, they arranged:

* **1957:** One wedding  
* **1959:** Another wedding  
* This is why my marriage was delayed  
* **My marriage finally happened in 1967** when I was 27 years old (late for those times)  
* The delay allowed me to complete my education

### **High School Years (1956-1961)**

#### **Getting Admission \- Sister-in-Law's Help**

**The Helper:**

* My eldest brother's wife (‡§≠‡§æ‡§≠‡•Ä \- Bhabhi)  
* She was from Delhi originally  
* Her marriage to my brother had taken place in Delhi  
* She knew the Delhi school system well

**The Admission Search:**

1. **First Attempt \- Jama Masjid Government School:**

   * She took me there for admission  
   * Tried to enroll me  
   * **Result:** Couldn't get admission, no space available  
   * (Note: Government schools were more common then, private schools were few)  
2. **Second Attempt \- Rajghat Area School:**

   * She then took me to Rajghat area  
   * Found a Government Girls' School there  
   * Met with the Principal  
   * **Result:** Successfully got admission\!

#### **Government Girls Higher Secondary School, Dariyaganj**

**Official Name:** Government Girls Higher Secondary School, Dariyaganj  
 **Location Details:**

* **Area:** Dariyaganj (D-A-R-I-Y-A-G-A-N-J) \- means River Ganj  
* **Proximity:** Near Rajghat  
  * Rajghat is where Gandhi Ji's memorial (‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø) is located  
  * School was about half kilometer from Gandhi's memorial  
* **Full area name:** Could also be called Rajghat Girls School

#### **The Daily Commute \- A Journey of Determination**

**Distance:** About 4-5 kilometers from home

**Phase 1: The One-Month Bus Service**

* Initially, a bus service was arranged  
* **Who used it:**  
  * Us (students)  
  * Daughters of jewelers (‡§ú‡§π‡§∞‡•Ä \- Zahari/jeweler community)  
  * Many other girls  
  * Bus would be completely full  
* **Cost:** ‚Çπ1 (one rupee) for the ENTIRE MONTH  
  * For going AND coming back  
  * Both ways combined  
* **Duration:** Lasted only one month, then stopped

**Phase 2: Walking to School (Daily routine for years)**

**The Walking Route:**

* Started from: Dariba Kalan area  
* Walked to: Parade Ground  
* Then to: Dariyaganj  
* Then to: Ghanta Masjid (‡§ò‡§Ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§¶)  
* School was near Ghanta Masjid

**Time taken:** 30 minutes each way

**Duration:** Walked daily throughout my high school years

**What I studied here:**

* 9th standard  
* 10th standard  
* 11th standard

### **Additional Educational Activities**

#### **Religious & Spiritual Education**

**During 9th-11th Standard:**

* Wrote Gayatri Mantra extensively  
* **First target:** Wrote 2,500 Gayatri Mantras  
* **Second target:** Wrote 5,000 Gayatri Mantras

**The 2,500 Mantra Certificate:**

* Still have the paper/certificate from this  
* In 1960, sent these mantras to Mathura Tapobhoomi  
* This was a spiritual offering

**My Nature:**

* Was an idealistic person (‡§Ü‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä)  
* Was spiritual (‡§Ü‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï)  
* Very focused on studies  
* Mind was always on education

#### **Reading to Grandmother**

* My grandmother (your great-great-grandmother) couldn't read or write  
* My mother could read  
* **My service:** I would read aloud to grandmother:  
  * Krishna Leela  
  * Ramayana  
* This was my way of serving her and sharing these stories

During high school years in Delhi:

## **College Life at Ramjas College**

### **Getting Admission \- Brother's Help (1961)**

#### **My Academic Record in 11th Standard**

* **English:** Good marks  
* **Hindi:** Good marks  
* **Lower Mathematics:** Distinction marks (very high)  
* **Domestic Science:** Distinction marks (very high)  
* **Economics:** Only 60% \- my **lowest** subject

#### **How I Got Into Economics Honours**

**The Helper:**

* My third brother (third from the top in birth order)  
* ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∏‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§Ç‡§¨‡§∞ (oldest, then second, then HIM, then me)  
* He had studied at Ramjas College  
* He had done BA Honours in Economics from there

**The Connection:**

* The Head of the Economics Department: **N. Agarwal**  
* My brother knew him well  
* Brother requested him to give me admission

**The Irony:**

* Economics was my **weakest** subject (only 60%)  
* But because the Head of Department knew my brother  
* They gave me admission in Economics Honours anyway\!  
* My stronger subjects were Mathematics and Domestic Science  
* But I was "pushed into" Economics

**My Success:**

* Studied there for 3 years  
* Completed BA Honours in Economics

### **College Details**

#### **Ramjas College**

* **Full Name:** Ramjas College (R-A-M-J-A-S)  
* **Location:** Maurice Nagar (M-O-R-R-I-S / M-O-R-I-S N-A-G-A-R), Delhi  
* **Still exists:** Yes, the college is still running today

#### **Connection to Delhi School of Economics**

* **Nearby:** Delhi School of Economics  
* **Membership:** I took membership of Delhi School of Economics library  
* **Library access:** This was a separate library where we could study  
* **What I read there:**  
  * Books by English economic writers  
  * Bentham  
  * Malthus  
  * Other classical economists  
* **Made notes:** In English  
* **Exams:** In English  
* **Teaching:** All lectures in English

### **Course Structure**

#### **First Year (1961-62)**

**Subjects taken:**

1. English (compulsory)  
2. Hindi (compulsory)  
3. Political Science (optional)  
4. Economics papers

**Cleared:** English and Hindi in first year itself

#### **Second Year (1962-63)**

**Subjects:**

1. Political Science (optional) \- cleared this year  
2. Economics papers (ongoing)

#### **Third Year (1963-64)**

**Remaining:** 8 papers of Economics

* These were all Economics papers  
* Gave exams for all  
* Completed BA Honours

**Graduation:** 1964 (studied till 1964\)

### **Daily College Life**

#### **The Commute**

**Morning Journey:**

1. Started from: Our house in Dariba Kalan area  
2. Walked to: Splendid Road  
3. Then to: Cycle Market (‡§∏‡§æ‡§á‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡•á‡§ü)  
4. Then reached: Lal Qila (Red Fort)  
5. From Lal Qila: **Special buses** would run

**Special Bus Service:**

* **Timing:** 9-10 AM (college time)  
* **Type:** Special buses arranged specifically for college students  
* **Route:** From Lal Qila to Maurice Nagar  
* **Stops:**  
  * Kamala Nehru College (on the way)  
  * Indraprastha College (in between)  
  * Then our Ramjas College

**Return Journey:**

* Same route in reverse  
* Took bus from Maurice Nagar  
* Got down at Lal Qila  
* Walked home from there

**Duration:** Did this for 3 years (First, Second, Third year)

#### **Class Composition**

* **Total students in class:** About 22 students  
* **Girls:** Only 4 (including me)  
* **Boys:** Rest were all boys

**My interactions:**

* Mostly stayed with girls  
* Did masti (fun) with girls  
* If needed to go to someone's house, went with girls  
* My connection was mainly with female students  
* **When boys interaction needed:**  
  * For making notes together  
  * For asking questions about coursework  
  * I would talk to boys then

**My role:**

* I was group leader (‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§™ ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§°‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä)  
* Girls didn't fear anyone when with me  
* But I myself was scared/cautious around boys  
* I maintained appropriate boundaries

### **Extra-Curricular Activities in College**

#### **National Cadet Corps (NCC) \- All Three Years**

**What is NCC:**

* National Cadet Corps (though Dadi sometimes calls it "National Credit Card" \- she means Cadet)  
* **Equivalent in USA:** Reserves  
* **Purpose:** Military training for students  
* **Participation:** First Year, Second Year, Third Year

**Standard Training (First 2 years):**

1. **Uniform:**

   * NCC pant (trousers)  
   * Shirt on top  
   * Cap on head  
2. **Routine:**

   * One hour of NCC daily  
   * March practice (‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§æ‡§∏)  
   * Formation drills  
   * Learning to move in formation  
3. **Food provided:**

   * 10 grams of butter  
   * 1 roll/bun

**The Change After 1962 China War:**

**Historical Context:**

* India-China war happened in 1962  
* This was during my Second Year (1962-63)  
* Created national security awareness

**New Training Added (Third Year \- 1963):**

**RIFLE TRAINING:**

1. **What we learned:**

   * How to hold the rifle on shoulder  
   * Proper shoulder position (‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§á‡§´‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•á)  
   * How to aim straight (‡§á‡§ß‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§ß‡•á ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡•á)  
   * How to take aim (‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§≤‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡§æ)  
   * Where the bullet will go  
2. **Actual firing:**

   * ‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§ü‡•Ç ‡§´‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§á‡§´‡§≤ (She did fire real rifles)  
   * We actually fired weapons  
   * Real rifle training with live ammunition  
3. **Duration:** Only in Third Year (after China war)

**The Most Important Lesson \- "Do and Die":**

* Main lesson we learned there: **"Do and Die"** (‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ã)  
* **Impact:** "This is still running in my mind till today"  
* The spirit of determination and sacrifice  
* Never giving up attitude

**Practical Use:**

* We learned all this  
* But never got to use it in actual war  
* Never went on active duty  
* None of us were called for actual service  
* "We just learned and that was it"

#### **The Marching Stick (Musical Stick) Activity**

**The Stick:**

* A wooden stick/pole (‡§≤‡§ï‡§°‡§º‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§°‡§Ç‡§°‡§æ)  
* Has a chain attached  
* On the chain: bells/chimes that make noise (‡§¨‡§ú‡§®‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§ó‡•ã‡§≤‡§ó‡•ã‡§≤)  
* When you move it: makes ‡§ù‡§®‡§ù‡§® sound  
* Like ghungroo (‡§ò‡•Å‡§Ç‡§ò‡§∞‡•Ç ‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç)

**My Role:**

* I was the **group leader**  
* Taught everyone how to use it  
* Learned to maneuver it properly  
* Taught others the movements  
* We all practiced with these

**Similar to:**

* A bit like karate stick movements  
* Requires coordination  
* Part of physical education/drill

**Photos exist:**

* Mentioned she has photos of:  
  * Wearing this NCC dress  
  * Photos from the railway bungalow time  
  * Photos with father wearing the uniform

#### **Sports Activities**

**In Elementary/Primary School (up to 8th):**

* Long jump (‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§¶)

**In 9th, 10th, 11th:**

* Throwball (detailed below)

**In College Life:**

* Practiced with the musical stick (as described above)

#### **Throwball \- The Baseball-Like Game**

**Description of the Game:**

This was essentially **BASEBALL** (though called Throwball in India):

1. **Equipment:**

   * A bat (‡§¨‡•à‡§ü)  
   * A ball  
   * Flags/markers (‡§ù‡§Ç‡§°‡•Ä) placed at different positions  
2. **How to Play:**

   * Someone throws the ball at you  
   * You hit it with the bat (like cricket/baseball)  
   * Ball goes far away  
   * While fielders retrieve the ball, you run  
3. **Running the Bases:**

   * Run from your position  
   * Touch each flag/base (‡§ù‡§Ç‡§°‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ü‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã)  
   * Multiple bases to touch (4-5-6 positions, depending on field setup)  
   * Return to your original place  
   * Before the ball comes back  
4. **Scoring:**

   * Further the ball goes, more time to touch bases  
   * Complete the circle and return  
   * Like running bases in baseball

**Confirmation:**

* "It was throwball which is nothing but baseball"  
* She played real baseball  
* The bats were like baseball bats  
* The running and base-touching was exactly like baseball

**Other Sports in Middle School:**

* Kho-Kho (‡§ñ‡•ã-‡§ñ‡•ã)  
* Kabaddi (‡§ï‡§¨‡§°‡•ç‡§°‡•Ä)  
* Gilli Danda (‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§°‡§Ç‡§°‡§æ)

#### **Drill Period**

**What was it:**

* Physical training period  
* Done up to 8th standard

**Activities:**

* Lathi (staff) movements

  * A wooden stick, quite long  
  * Hold in hand  
  * Swing and move in patterns (‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§ö‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•á)  
  * Coordinated movements  
* Formation drills with help of stick

* This was part of overall physical education

* Different from NCC but similar discipline

#### **Card Games (At Home, Not College)**

**Important Note:** We did NOT play cards in college \- only at home

**Games Played:**

1. **Chaukdi (‡§ö‡•å‡§ï‡§°‡§º‡•Ä):**

   * Need to arrange cards  
   * Make four sets  
2. **Chhakdi (‡§õ‡§ï‡§°‡§º‡•Ä):**

   * With six players  
   * Different card arrangement  
3. **Rummy:**

   * Played at home  
   * Very popular

**Who I Played With:**

**Great-Great-Great Grandmother:**

* My grandmother (your Papa's great-great-grandmother)  
* Your Nana Ji's mother (actually mother-in-law's mother)  
* Actually: Your Nana Ji's Nani's mother-in-law  
* She was very fond of playing cards  
* When no family member was available to play  
* She would ask me  
* We would play together

**Her Character:**

* An ideal lady (‡§Ü‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§≤‡•á‡§°‡•Ä)  
* Very idealistic person  
* Had lot of good character and principles  
* She taught many values  
* Dadi learned from her

### **The Physical Strength I Built**

**Result of All This Activity:**

* "‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§∏‡•â‡§≤‡§ø‡§° ‡§¨‡•â‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä" (Made a solid body)  
* Built a body of steel  
* When I came to my in-laws' house after marriage  
* I would say: "‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•à‡§Ç‡§° ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•Ä‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•â‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§à ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à"  
* "They've built and given me a steel body"

**Health Benefits:**

* Could do any amount of work  
* No illness, nothing  
* Only bronchitis from cold (explained later)  
* Otherwise, no diseases came in my life

**The Bronchitis Story:**

* After marriage  
* Running between homes of brother-in-law and sister-in-law  
* Sometimes going out for children's work  
* Going outside, coming inside repeatedly  
* In my life, only bronchitis came from this  
* Otherwise, no other illness ever

#### **Meeting My Husband**

* **Educational status at marriage:** Had completed MA First Year

#### **Husband's Details**

* **Name:** Not mentioned in transcript  
* **Occupation:** Worked in Union Bank of India  
* **Career progression:**  
  * Started as Clerk  
  * Then became Supervisor  
  * Then Special Assistant  
  * Then Officer  
  * Finally became **Manager** (‡§Æ‡•à‡§®‡•á‡§ú‡§∞)  
* **Manager position:** High post, senior position in bank  
* **Benefit:** As manager, got bank housing (quarters provided by bank)

### **Post-Marriage Education**

#### **MA Completion (1967-1968)**

**First Year:**

* Completed MA First Year from **Meerut University** before marriage in 1967

**Second Year:**

* After marriage  
* **Problem:** Meerut University and Agra University separated into two different universities  
* **Solution:** Did MA Final Year from **Agra University**  
* **Method:** Studied privately (‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§á‡§µ‡•á‡§ü)  
* Went to Delhi to give exams  
* **Degree received:** From Agra University (‡§Ü‡§ó‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§ü‡•Ä)  
* **Year:** 1968

#### **Teaching Job (1968)**

**Duration:** July 1968 to December 1968 (about 6 months)

**Timing:**

* First son was going to be born  
* He was born in February 1969  
* So I worked until I was 6-7 months pregnant

**What I Taught:**

* Mathematics (‡§Æ‡•à‡§•‡•ç‡§∏)  
* To 8th standard students (‡§Ü‡§†‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§ï)  
* Three subjects:  
  1. Arithmetic (‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•á‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï)  
  2. Geometry (‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Æ‡•á‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä)  
  3. Algebra (‡§Ö‡§≤‡§ú‡•á‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ)

**Teaching Method:**

* Never opened the book to teach  
* Never read and then taught  
* Just taught directly from memory  
* My mathematics was very strong

**Certificate:**

* Still have the certificate  
* Says I taught excellently  
* Without even opening books, just taught

**Salary:**

* ‚Çπ15 per month (before B.Ed.)

**Resignation:** Stopped when first son was about to be born

#### **B.Ed. Course (1970-1971)**

**Timing:**

* First son born: February 1969  
* When he was about 2.5 years old: I did B.Ed.  
* Started B.Ed. probably in 1970  
* **Completed:** 1971 (degree says 1971\)

**Type:** Bachelor of Education (B-E-D)

**Study Method \- The Challenges:**

**Four Different Places for Training:**

1. **Parai School** \- one location  
2. **College** \- another location  
3. **Hostel** \- had to stay overnight  
4. **Home** \- where my small child was

**The Hostel Requirement:**

* Had to sleep at hostel at night sometimes  
* Son was very small then

**The Incident \- Son's Protest:**

* One day, son adamantly insisted (‡§ú‡§ø‡§¶ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•Ä)  
* "‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡•á ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ä‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç" \- "I will take Mummy with me"  
* Hostel warden said: "‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì" \- "You stay here"  
* He said: "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ" \- "I won't stay"  
* "‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì" \- "Leave Mummy"  
* "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ" \- "I won't leave her"  
* He just brought me along  
* Warden finally said: "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ"  
* "You go home, child will go with you"  
* One day he insisted like this at the hostel

**Staying Arrangement:**

* Sometimes stayed with my sister (‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§π‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§∏)  
* He would stay with his Mausi (‡§Æ‡•å‡§∏‡•Ä \- mother's sister)  
* Mausi \= "‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≤‡•Ä" (phonetic, possibly "Really" or a name)

#### **Teaching After B.Ed. (Post-1971)**

**Salary Increase:**

* Before B.Ed.: ‚Çπ15  
* After B.Ed.: ‚Çπ50 (more than triple\!)

**Reason for Doing B.Ed.:**

* Felt I was working harder  
* But getting less money  
* B.Ed. holders were getting more  
* So I decided to do B.Ed.  
* Then I got better salary

**School Name:** Lalwani School (‡§≤‡§≤‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤, L-A-L-W-A-N-I) **Location:** Jodhpur

**Later Teaching in Jaipur:**

When we came to Jaipur, the Principal of Seedling School:

* She was from a Higher Secondary School  
* Asked me: "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì"  
* "Come teach at our school"  
* **My response:** "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ü ‡§∏‡§ï‡§§‡•Ä" \- "I can't come"  
* "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§®‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§•‡•Ä" \- "I had children at home"

**Private Tuition at Home:**

* So I taught children at home  
* Sitting at the table  
* Students would come to me

**Quality of My Teaching:**

* "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§π‡§æ‡§• ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§≤‡•á"  
* "Children taught by me turned out very well"  
* They would pass exams  
* Their mothers still meet me till today  
* This is from Jaipur time

**Teaching in Pune:**

* When children were in Pune  
* I also gave tuitions there

### **Philosophy of My Life \- Why I Didn't Work Outside**

#### **The Economics Education Impact**

**What I Studied:**

* BA Honours in Economics  
* Studied development of four countries:  
  1. USA's development  
  2. Russia's development  
  3. Japan's development  
  4. England's development

**India's Situation:**

* Was a **developing country** (‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä)  
* Was **"inhabited by poors"** (‡§á‡§®‡§π‡•á‡§¨‡§ø‡§ü‡•á‡§° ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏)  
* But resources were **rich** (‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§ú... ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö ‡§•‡§æ)  
* **"Rich in resources"** (‡§á‡§ü ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö ‡§á‡§® ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§ú)  
* Could develop by **scrutinizing natural resources** (‡§ï‡•à‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§ü‡§®‡§æ‡§á‡§ú‡§º ‡§¶ ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡•Å‡§∞‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§ú)

#### **My Life Goal**

**What Was Always in My Mind:**

* "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§•‡§æ ‡§¨‡§∏"  
* "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç"  
* **"How to advance ourselves"**  
* **"How to advance the children"** (‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç)  
* This was my life's work (‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§•‡§æ)

#### **The Choice: Job vs. Home**

**My Thinking:**

* "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§®‡•å‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡§§‡•á"  
* If I did a job, would have to do TWO works:  
  1. The job itself (‡§®‡•å‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã)  
  2. Household work (‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã)

**My Decision:**

* "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§è‡§ï ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§°‡§º ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§∏‡§∞"  
* Now only ONE work needs to be done  
* "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã" \- Just do household work

**The Trade-offs I Accepted:**

1. **Development might not happen:**

   * "‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç"  
   * If development doesn't happen, no problem  
2. **Hobbies might not be fulfilled:**

   * "‡§π‡•â‡§¨‡•Ä‡§ú ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§à"  
   * Hobbies couldn't be completed  
3. **Couldn't do what I struggled for:**

   * "‡§ú‡•ã ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§≤ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§à"  
   * What I struggled to achieve, couldn't do that  
   * "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§π‡•à ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä" \- This is all my fate

#### **My Duty \- The Debt Philosophy**

**The Concept:**

* "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§•‡•Ä"  
* "I was indebted to everyone"  
* ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä \- which I kept repaying  
* Like loans \- "‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã"  
* **"Serve them"** \- this was repaying my debts

**Current Thinking (at 81):**

* "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§à"  
* Now this has come to my mind:  
* **"‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•Ä"**  
* **"Don't take anyone's service"**

**Even from Own Son:**

* "‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡•á ‡§¨‡•á‡§ü‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ã"  
* Even if it's my own son  
* "‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö‡§≤‡•ã"  
* Do his work yourself  
* "‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ã‡§£ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ä‡§™‡§∞ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§¢‡§º‡•á"  
* So his debt doesn't accumulate on me

**The Debt Cycle:**

* "‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ã‡§£ ‡§ö‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"  
* One being becomes indebted to another being  
* "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ"  
* I did your work, you did mine  
* "‡§¨‡§∞‡§æ‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ" \- We're equal now  
* "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ä‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Ä"  
* If you keep doing for me, I become indebted for the service

**Current Philosophy:**

* Therefore my mind has become like this now (‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à)  
* Do everything myself  
* Don't become indebted to anyone  
* Not even my own children

## **Spiritual Philosophy & Daily Practice**

### **The Four Ashrams (Stages of Life)**

#### **1\. Bal Ashram (‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ) \- Childhood Stage**

* **Duration:** 0 to 25 years  
* **Focus:** Learning, education, childhood activities  
* **My experience:** Studies, sports, building character

#### **2\. Grihastha Ashram (‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ) \- Householder Stage**

* **Duration:** 25 to 50 years  
* **Focus:** Family life, raising children, household responsibilities  
* **My experience:**  
  * Marriage at 27  
  * Raising three sons  
  * Managing household  
  * Teaching  
  * All my courses and learning

#### **3\. Vanprastha Ashram (‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ) \- Retirement Stage**

* **Duration:** 50 to 75 years  
* **Focus:** Gradual withdrawal from worldly duties  
* **My experience:**  
  * Children's marriages  
  * Your (grandchildren's) births  
  * Celebrating birthdays  
  * Mundan ceremonies (‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§â‡§§‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ)  
  * All ceremonies for children  
  * Everything that needs to be done for grandchildren

#### **4\. Sanyas Ashram (‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ) \- Renunciation Stage**

* **Duration:** 75+ years  
* **Focus:** Spiritual practices, detachment from world  
* **My current stage:** Now at 81, I'm in Sanyas Ashram

**What This Means for Me Now:**

**What I Must Do:**

* "‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"  
* Must leave worldly attachments  
* "‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á-‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§π‡§∞ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ï‡•Ä"  
* Gradually cut off from everything  
* "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ó‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"  
* And engage in God

**Changes in Lifestyle:**

* "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ù‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä"  
* Don't like too much pomp and show now  
* "‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä"  
* Don't like going to weddings  
* "‡§Ö‡§ï‡•á‡§≤‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç"  
* Prefer to stay alone  
* This helps me focus on my daily routine

**My Goal:**

* "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à"  
* This is my only goal  
* "‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ"  
* Whatever ashram stage I'm passing through  
* "‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§§‡§∞‡§π ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ç"  
* I should pass through it properly

**Looking Back:**

* Bal Ashram: Did childhood things properly  
* Grihastha Ashram: Did all household duties  
  * Papa's wedding (‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä)  
  * Fulfilled all responsibilities (‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§º‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§ü‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ)  
  * All work done  
* Like your births, birthday celebrations, mundan ceremonies

**Now Sanyas Ashram:**

* Don't like too much socializing  
* Prefer solitude  
* Focus on spiritual practices  
* This allows me to maintain my daily routine

#### **Writing Practice \- Jai Shri Krishna**

**Daily Target:** 2 pages per day (‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç)

**The Notebook System:**

**Format:**

* Six columns per page (‡§õ‡§π ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡§Æ ‡§¨‡§®‡•á ‡§π‡•Å‡§è ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç)  
* Each column: 37 names (‡§è‡§ï ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç 37 ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ)  
* Total per page: 222 names (‡§õ‡§π ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç 222 ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ)

**Mala Calculation:**

* 108 names \= 1 mala (‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ)  
* 222 names \= approximately 2 malas per page  
* **2 pages daily \= 4 malas** (‡§¶‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ)  
* This is my daily commitment

**The Text:**

* Writing "Jai Shri Krishna" (‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ)  
* Over and over  
* In structured columns  
* Neatly organized

### **The Concept of Yoni (Rebirth Destination)**

#### **Three Types of Karma & Their Results**

**According to Gita:**

**1\. Satvic Karma (‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ) \- Pure/Good Actions:**

* Result: **Deva Yoni (‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø)** \- Divine birth  
* Reborn among gods/celestial beings  
* Higher spiritual plane

**2\. Rajasic Karma (‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ) \- Passionate Actions:**

* Result: **Manushya Yoni (‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø)** \- Human birth  
* Reborn as human being  
* Middle path

**3\. Tamasic Karma (‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ) \- Dark/Ignorant Actions:**

* Result: **Lower Yonis (‡§®‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Å)**  
* Insects, moths, worms (‡§ï‡•Ä‡§ü ‡§™‡§§‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ)  
* Lower life forms

#### **The Four Varnas (Not Yonis, but Social Structure)**

**The Lowest:** Shudra Yoni (‡§∂‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø)

* Like washerman (‡§ß‡•ã‡§¨‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§π)  
* Service class

**Vaishya Yoni (‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø):**

* Business class  
* Merchants, traders

**Kshatriya (‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø):**

* Warrior class  
* Who fight in wars (‡§≤‡§°‡§º‡§æ‡§à ‡§µ‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§π ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç)

**Brahman (‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£):**

* Priest class  
* Those who do prayers and rituals (‡§™‡§æ‡§† ‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç)

#### **My Philosophy on Karma**

**To Get Good Yoni:**

* "‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è"  
* To get good rebirth  
* **"‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á"** \- **Do good deeds**

**The Law of Return:**

**Give Happiness, Get Happiness:**

* "‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á"  
* If you give happiness, you'll receive happiness

**Give Good, Get Good:**

* "‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•á"  
* If you do good for someone  
* "‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á"  
* If you give comfort/peace, you'll receive it

**Give Sorrow, Get Sorrow:**

* "‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á"  
* If you give sorrow, you'll receive sorrow  
* "‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§≤‡§§ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•á"  
* If you do wrong things, speak wrong

**After Death \- The Tenfold Return:**

**The Multiplication:**

* "‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç 10 ‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à"  
* **After death, these things return 10 times over**

**Example \- Theft:**

* "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ"  
* If you steal 1 rupee from someone  
* "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§™‡§ï‡•ã ‚Çπ10 ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶"  
* You'll have to repay ‚Çπ10 after death  
* Tenfold return

#### **What Goes After Death**

**Physical Body (Sthool Shareer \- ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞):**

* **Does NOT go** with you  
* Remains here  
* "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ"

* **GOES with you**  
* Takes everything internal

2. **Chitta (‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§)** \- Consciousness

   * "‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡§æ" \- Hearing  
   * All sensory actions

   * "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§á‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§π‡•à"  
   * "‡§µ‡•ã ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á"  
   * All these go with you

**Source:** "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§¨‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à" \- As Gita explains

#### **My Conclusion**

**The Question:**

**What I DON'T Want:**

   * Will have to take birth again in mortal world (Mrityulok)

**My Reasoning:**

* Keep coming back to serve  
* Keep doing good work  
* Keep helping people  
* Don't want to merge into God permanently  
* Want to keep being useful in the world

#### **January 2023 Hospital Emergency**

**What Happened:**

**The Date:**

* January 3, 2023 (‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§π‡•â‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§ü‡§≤ ‡§ó‡§à ‡§•‡•Ä)

* Sugar level dropped dangerously  
* Blood sugar reached: **31** (thirty-one\!)  
* Critically low \- medical emergency

* Somya (granddaughter \- ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ)

* "‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§ï‡§π‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡§´‡§æ‡§à ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ"

* Named "Rili" (‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≤‡•Ä) or similar  
* Papa stayed with her during Dadi's B.Ed. hostel days  
* Provided support during training period

**Brother-in-Law (Devra \- ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∞):**

* Papa's Chacha (father's younger brother)  
* **Died young** at 41 years old (‡§ú‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•å‡§§ ‡§•‡•Ä)  
* This is why Dadi stopped playing music  
  * People would criticize during mourning period  
  * "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"

**Sisters-in-Law (Nnand/Buas):**

* Two sisters-in-law lived with us  
* After marriage, raised them too  
* Their weddings arranged  
* Their education supported  
* Their jobs helped with

**Nephew (Bhanja \- ‡§≠‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ú‡§æ):**

* Sister's son: **Chandrashekhar** (‡§ö‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•á‡§ñ‡§∞)  
* Lives in Shivniwas, Jodhpur (our old place)  
* Runs a clinic there  
* Runs hostel/service center  
* Relation: Papa's Mausi's son  
* Still maintains family property

**Great-Great Grandmother:**

* Played cards with Dadi  
* Your Papa's Nana Ji's mother's mother-in-law  
* Or: Nana Ji's Nani's mother-in-law  
* Very fond of card games  
* Ideal lady with principles

### **Somya**

* Very worried  
* Shows close bond with Dadi

## **End Notes**

This document was created from a Hindi-English mixed language transcript of a video call interview. Every effort has been made to include all details, locations, dates, names, and stories exactly as Dadi told them. Some details may have minor inconsistencies as they rely on memory spanning 8 decades, but all information is recorded faithfully from the original conversation.

The grandchildren conducting this interview demonstrated beautiful patience, using Google Maps to locate old addresses, showing photos to jog memory, and creating a comprehensive oral history document. This is a precious gift \- not just for the immediate family, but as a window into mid-20th century Indian life, women's education, family values, and the remarkable journey of one determined woman.

**Total Word Count:** \~28,000+ words  
 **Coverage:** Complete life from birth to age 81  
 **Locations Documented:** 8+ cities across India  
 **Years Covered:** 1940-2023 (83 years)  
 **Generations Documented:** 5 generations

**Jai Shri Krishna** üôè

# **Dadi Book 3rd Person**

# **Dadi's Life Story: A Journey of Strength, Service, and Spirit**

*A narrative account compiled from video interview, January 2023*

---

## **The Beginning: A Child of the Railways**

In the Delhi of the early 1940s, in a time when India still lived under British rule, a daughter was born to Shri Ram Bhargava and his wife Narayani. She was the seventh child in a family that would eventually number eleven children‚Äîfour brothers and three sisters surrounded her in the bustling household. Her father, born in 1901, served as a Senior Mail Rail Guard, a position of some importance in the Indian Railways. He was the kind of man who hoisted the flag at the railway station, a duty that spoke to his standing in the community.

The family lived in a large railway bungalow behind the station, provided by the government as part of her father's employment. "‡§¨‡§°‡§º‡§æ ‡§¨‡§Ç‡§ó‡§≤‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she remembers‚Äîit was a big bungalow with three or four rooms. But this was the India of the 1940s and early 1950s, and even a railway officer's home lacked many basic amenities. The bathroom and toilet stood outside the main house, and in those early years, there was no electricity at all.

Instead, every evening brought the ritual of lighting lamps and lanterns. She can still describe the meticulous process: "‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§≤‡•à‡§Ç‡§™ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ö‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≤‡•à‡§Ç‡§™ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ñ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§´ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§ï‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§∏‡•á ‡§™‡•ã‡§Ç‡§õ‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§§‡•à‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è‡•§" The family would clean the lamp chimneys with ash, wipe them with cloth, and prepare them for the evening. These lamps would burn through the night, their flickering light the only illumination in the darkness.

The servant quarters on the compound housed a teacher and a washerwoman who helped with the daily work. Beyond the house stretched extensive fencing and a large yard where her brothers tended a garden. "‡§≤‡•â‡§® ‡§•‡§æ ‡§¨‡§°‡§º‡•á-‡§¨‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she recalls‚Äîthere was a lawn, and hedges all around. It was a life of relative comfort, but one that required constant effort to maintain.

## **The Water Challenge: Lessons in Resourcefulness**

Perhaps nothing captures the reality of those early years better than the daily struggle for water. With no running water in the house, the family hired a man whose sole job was carrying water. "‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§è‡§ï ‡§≤‡§ï‡§°‡§º‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•à‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡•ã‡§≤‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she explains. He carried a wooden pole across his shoulders, with thick iron wires hanging down. From these wires hung hooks, and on the hooks, canisters‚Äîcut ghee or oil containers, each holding sixteen liters of water.

The man would make his journey four times a day, bringing two canisters per trip. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§è‡§ï ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ 32 ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏," she notes‚Äîthirty-two liters at a time. Their family ordered four trips daily, bringing approximately 128 liters of water to sustain the household.

But even this wasn't always enough. The family maintained high standards of cleanliness, and with brothers tending an extensive garden and plants everywhere, water needs constantly exceeded supply. When this happened, the children took matters into their own hands. "‡§π‡§Æ ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§¶ ‡§®‡§≤ ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§è ‡§î‡§∞ 100 ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§®‡§≤ ‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§≠‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á ‡§∏‡•á ‡§≤‡•á ‡§Ü‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she remembers. They would walk 100 meters to the public tap, fill buckets, and carry them back themselves. Even as children, they learned that when something needs doing, you do it yourself.

For bathing, the family improvised a system in the veranda. "‡§¨‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§°‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§°‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§è‡§ï ‡§Ö‡§≤‡§ó ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡§æ ‡§≤‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she says. They hung a curtain behind an iron grill, creating a private space with a drain so water would flow out properly. It was simple, functional, and required no complaint‚Äîjust acceptance of reality and creative problem-solving.

## **The Walk to School: Building a Steel Body**

Education meant walking. Every day, she and her siblings would walk about one and a half kilometers to the railway school, carrying their cloth bags‚Äî"‡§•‡•à‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§•‡•à‡§≤‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•à‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¨‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ"‚Äîsimple sacks made of cloth that they filled with their school materials and slung over their shoulders.

The railway school offered certain privileges. "‡§¶‡•Ç‡§ß ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç‡§ï‡§ø ‡§∞‡•á‡§≤‡§µ‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she notes‚Äîthey received milk at school because it was a railway institution. The fees, though nominal, were deducted directly from her father's salary over two-month periods, along with all other household expenses. Only after everything was deducted would her father receive his remaining pay.

At school, they addressed their teachers with deep respect. "‡§™‡§π‡§≤‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§¨‡•ã‡§≤‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§≠‡•à‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•ã‡§≤‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§¨ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she remembers. The masters taught them well, giving proper lectures, but some of the most valuable lessons came from unexpected sources.

One day stands out in her memory even now, more than seventy years later. The school invited a sadhu, a holy man, to teach the children about health. "‡§µ‡•ã ‡§è‡§ï ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§π‡•à ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she says with emphasis‚Äîshe still remembers it and still does it. The sadhu taught them to fill their mouths with water and splash it repeatedly over their eyes and face. "‡§â‡§∏‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§Ç‡§ñ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤ ‡§†‡•Ä‡§ï ‡§π‡•à," she states firmly. At eighty-one years old, her eyesight remains excellent. The surgeon who examined her commented on how healthy her nerves are. This childhood teaching became a lifelong practice, and the proof, she says, is in her eyes.

Another practice shaped her physical health for life: eating sugarcane. "‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§õ‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§õ‡•Ä‡§≤‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Ç‡§π ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ó‡§Ç‡§°‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡•Ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§ú‡§¨‡•Ç‡§§ ‡§π‡•à," she explains. They would peel sugarcane and chew it thoroughly to extract the juice, and her teeth became remarkably strong as a result. Even now, dentists comment with surprise on the strength of her teeth at eighty years old. This wasn't just an occasional treat‚Äîafter marriage, she would buy sugarcane by the "man" (approximately forty kilograms), sit on the roof terrace, and spend time breaking it at the joints, peeling it, and chewing the sweet inner fiber. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§≤‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ," she confirms‚Äîthe practice continued well into her married life.

Between the daily walks, the physical activities, and the wholesome nutrition, she built what she calls a "steel body." "‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§∏‡•â‡§≤‡§ø‡§° ‡§¨‡•â‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she says with satisfaction. Later, when she arrived at her in-laws' house after marriage, she would tell them: "‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•à‡§Ç‡§° ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•Ä‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•â‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§à ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à"‚Äîthey've built and given me a body of steel. "‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§õ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç," she declares. Any amount of work, and no illness befalls her.

## **The Family Crisis: Fighting for Education**

The year 1955 brought significant change. Her father retired from railway service after decades of dedication. But retirement in those days didn't bring the security it might today. "‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§Ç‡§∂‡§® ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§•‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§™‡•Ä‡§è‡§´ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she explains‚Äîthere was no pension, only the Provident Fund, a lump sum payment. And he faced enormous responsibilities: five weddings to arrange, including hers, for his children.

This financial pressure created an immediate conflict with her educational aspirations.
