Moving back to their family home in Delhi‚Äî"152 ‡§ï‡§ü‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Æ, ‡§¶‡§∞‡•Ä‡§¨‡§æ ‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§®, ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•Ä," a massive house with twenty-two to twenty-four rooms arranged around a central courtyard‚Äîshould have meant opportunity. Her grandfather had purchased this ancestral home some eighty-six years before her birth. But in 1956, at age sixteen, she found herself fighting for something many families didn't consider essential: continued education for a daughter.

"‡§π‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á," she insisted firmly‚ÄîI will study. The resistance wasn't merely about money. Girls' education wasn't always encouraged in those times. Society had different expectations. But she refused to accept this limitation. "‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§à ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§∞‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§•‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§≤ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡§æ," she acknowledges‚Äîshe had to struggle for this, especially for college education. Her father wasn't ready, the family hesitated, but she stood firm.

Eventually, her father‚Äîthis man born in 1901, her great-great-grandfather in the family tree‚Äîgave his permission. "‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ó‡§µ ‡§π‡§∞ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®," she says. This was progressive thinking for that era, and she has never forgotten that he ultimately supported her dreams. To manage finances, the family arranged two weddings in 1957 and 1959\. Her own marriage would wait until 1967, when she was twenty-seven‚Äîextraordinarily late for those times, but it allowed her to complete her education.

## **Delhi Days: The Daily Journey to Knowledge**

Getting into high school required help. Her eldest brother's wife, a Delhi native familiar with the school system, became her advocate. They first tried the Government school near Jama Masjid. "‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§¶ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ó‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§•‡§æ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§à ‡§•‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§π ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä," she recalls‚Äîno space available. Government schools were more common then, private schools fewer, but this meant admission could be competitive.

Her sister-in-law tried again, this time at a Government Girls' School in the Rajghat area, not far from where Gandhi Ji's memorial stands. "‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ò‡§æ‡§ü ‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ó‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§π‡•à‡•§ ‡§â‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§æ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§®‡•á ‡§è‡§°‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡§® ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§™‡§≤ ‡§∏‡•á," she remembers. The principal agreed, and she was enrolled at what would officially be called Government Girls Higher Secondary School, Dariyaganj.

The school lay approximately four to five kilometers from her home in Dariba Kalan. "‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä‡§¨ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ò‡§æ‡§ü ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ã ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ó‡§à," she notes. For one brief month, she experienced the luxury of bus transportation. A bus service was arranged specifically for the girls‚Äîstudents and daughters of jewelers, filling the vehicle completely. The cost was remarkably modest: "‚Çπ1 ‡§≤‡•á‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§â‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ"‚Äîone rupee for the entire month, for both going and coming.

But after just one month, "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§™‡•à‡§¶‡§≤ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she says‚Äîthe bus stopped and they walked. Every single day, for years, she walked the route: from Dariba Kalan to Parade Ground, then to Dariyaganj, past Ghanta Masjid, to her school near Rajghat. "‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§ß‡§æ ‡§ò‡§Ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§≤‡§ó‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she recalls‚Äîthirty minutes each way. This wasn't seen as a hardship. It was simply what one did. The walk built strength, discipline, and determination.

During these years, from ninth through eleventh standard, her mind stayed focused on studies. "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§à ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she emphasizes. But she wasn't merely bookish. Her spiritual side flourished too. During ninth and eleventh standards, she wrote the Gayatri Mantra thousands of times‚Äîfirst 2,500, then 5,000 repetitions. "‡§¢‡§æ‡§à ‡§π‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ó‡§ú ‡§π‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§® 60 ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§¢‡§æ‡§à ‡§π‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§≠‡•á‡§ú‡•á," she says. She still possesses the certificate from 1960 showing she sent 2,500 mantras to Mathura Tapobhoomi as a spiritual offering.

"‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¢‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£," she remembers. She was idealistic, spiritually inclined. Her grandmother couldn't read, so she would read aloud the Krishna Leela and Ramayana to her‚Äîan act of service and devotion combined.

## **College: Breaking Barriers**

When the time came for college, she faced an ironic situation. Her academic record in eleventh standard showed distinction marks in Lower Mathematics and Domestic Science, good marks in English and Hindi, but only sixty percent in Economics‚Äîher weakest subject. "Economics ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§Æ ‡§®‡§Ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§•‡•á," she admits frankly.

Yet Economics was exactly where she ended up, thanks to her third brother. "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§•‡•á," she explains‚Äîshe had four brothers, and the third one had studied at Ramjas College in Maurice Nagar, Delhi. He had completed BA Honours in Economics there and knew the Head of Department, N. Agarwal. "‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•ã‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§è‡§°‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡§® ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§î‡§∞ Economics ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¢‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§¨‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§Æ ‡§®‡§Ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§è ‡§•‡•á," she says with a laugh‚Äîthey got her admission and "pushed" her into Economics despite it being her weakest subject.

The irony didn't defeat her. She studied at Ramjas College for three years, from 1961 to 1964, completing her BA Honours. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•Ä," she confirms. The teaching was entirely in English, exams in English, and she took membership at the nearby Delhi School of Economics library. There she read the English economic writers‚ÄîBentham, Malthus, and others‚Äîmaking notes in English, absorbing theories of development that would shape her worldview for life.

"‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§Ø‡•Ç ‡§è‡§∏ ‡§è ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§∞‡§∂‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§≤‡•à‡§Ç‡§° ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she reflects. She studied the development of the USA, Russia, Japan, and England. Meanwhile, "‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ India ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§•‡§æ ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§•‡§æ"‚ÄîIndia was a developing country, "‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö ‡§á‡§® ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§ú ‡§è‡§Ç‡§° ‡§á‡§®‡§π‡•à‡§¨‡§ø‡§ü‡•á‡§° ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏"‚Äîrich in resources but inhabited by poor people. The question that formed in her mind would guide her entire life: "‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç"‚Äîhow to advance ourselves, how to advance our children.

Her commute to Ramjas involved walking from Dariba Kalan to Splendid Road, then to Cycle Market, reaching Lal Qila where special buses ran during college hours‚Äî9 to 10 AM‚Äîcarrying students to Maurice Nagar. "‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§≠‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she remembers‚Äîthe bus would be completely full, stopping at Kamala Nehru College and Indraprastha College before reaching Ramjas.

In her class of about twenty-two students, only four were girls. "‡§π‡§Æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§°‡§º‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§•‡•á ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡•á‡§ú ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§¶‡§∞ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§≤‡§°‡§º‡§ï‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she notes. "‡§≤‡§°‡§º‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§™‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§¨‡§∏," she says‚Äîthe girls had fun among themselves. When she needed to discuss notes or ask questions about coursework, she would speak with the boys, but her main connections were with fellow female students. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§™ ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§°‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she states proudly‚Äîshe was always the group leader. The girls didn't fear anything when she was around, though she herself remained appropriately cautious around boys.

## **NCC: Learning "Do or Die"**

College brought an experience that would mark her permanently: the National Cadet Corps. For three years‚Äîfirst year, second year, and third year‚Äîshe participated in NCC training. "‡§´‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü ‡§à‡§Ø‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç‡§° ‡§à‡§Ø‡§∞ ‡§•‡§∞‡•ç‡§° ‡§à‡§Ø‡§∞ NCC ‡§•‡•Ä," she confirms.

The standard training involved wearing a uniform‚ÄîNCC pants and shirt with a cap‚Äîand drilling for an hour daily. "‡§è‡§ï ‡§ò‡§Ç‡§ü‡§æ NCC ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she recalls. They learned to march in formation, received 10 grams of butter and a roll each session, and practiced coordinated movements with various implements including a musical stick‚Äîa wooden rod with chains and bells that would chime as they maneuvered it. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§™ ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§°‡§∞ ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§â‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she notes‚Äîshe was group leader for this too, teaching everyone the movements.

But everything changed after 1962\. "‡§ú‡§¨ China ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§≤‡§°‡§º‡§æ‡§à ‡§π‡•Å‡§à 62 ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ã 63 ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•ã‡§Ç‡§®‡•á rifle training ‡§¶‡•Ä," she explains. The India-China war brought a new intensity to their training. In her third year, they learned actual rifle handling. "‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡§∞ rifle ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§á‡§ß‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§ß‡•á ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡•á ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§≤‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ," she describes‚Äîhow to hold the rifle on the shoulder, how to take aim, where the bullet would go. "‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§ü‡•Ç ‡§´‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§≤ rifle," she confirms emphatically‚Äîshe actually fired real rifles.

The practical application never came. "‡§™‡§∞ ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü‡•§ ‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§∞‡§π ‡§ó‡§è," she admits‚Äîthey learned but never used it in actual service. Yet something more important stayed with her. "‡§™‡§∞ ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§è‡§ï ‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§ ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§ñ‡•á '‡§°‡•Ç ‡§è‡§Ç‡§° ‡§°‡§æ‡§à' ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she declares with feeling. The main lesson learned there‚Äî"Do or Die"‚Äîstill runs in her mind today. That spirit of determination, of never giving up, of being willing to sacrifice everything for what matters‚Äîthis became part of her character.

She also played sports. "‡§•‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§¨‡•â‡§≤ ‡§ñ‡•á‡§≤‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á," she says, describing what was essentially baseball‚Äîsomeone throws the ball, you hit it with a bat, it goes far, and while fielders retrieve it, you run touching flags or bases before returning to your position. "‡§•‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§¨‡•â‡§≤ ‡§á‡§ú ‡§®‡§•‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§¨‡§ü ‡§¨‡•á‡§∏‡§¨‡•â‡§≤," she confirms with a smile. "‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§° ‡§¨‡•á‡§∏‡§¨‡•â‡§≤," as her grandson summarizes. Between the physical training, the rifle practice, the marching drills, the sports, and the daily walking, she built extraordinary physical strength.

## **The Journey Continues: Marriage and Teaching**

By 1967, she had completed her MA First Year from Meerut University. When Meerut and Agra Universities separated, she completed her MA Final Year through Agra University privately, traveling to Delhi to give exams. Her degree came from Agra University in 1968\. That same year, newly married at the late age of twenty-seven, she took her first teaching position.

From July to December 1968, while pregnant with her first son, she taught mathematics to eighth standard students. "‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•á‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Æ‡•á‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§≤‡§ú‡•á‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨‡•ç‡§ú‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§ü ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she lists‚Äîarithmetic, geometry, and algebra, all three subjects. Her teaching method was remarkable: "‡§¨‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§ñ‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§õ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§¨ ‡§ñ‡•ã‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¢‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she emphasizes. She never opened the book to teach, never read and then taught‚Äîjust taught directly from her understanding. "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§• ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she states simply. Her mathematics was very strong. She still possesses the certificate stating she taught excellently.

But the salary was modest‚Äîfifteen rupees per month. "‡§™‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§ï‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á," she thought‚Äîtoo little money for the hard work. Others with B.Ed. degrees earned more, so she decided to get the qualification herself.

The B.Ed. course in 1970-71 presented challenges. She had to manage four different locations: a Parai school, a college, a hostel where she sometimes stayed overnight, and her home where her small son waited. "‡§è‡§ï ‡§¶‡§ø‡§® ‡§ú‡§ø‡§¶ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•ã‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡•á ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ä‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç," she remembers with a laugh. One day her son insisted at the hostel: I will take Mummy with me, I won't leave without her. The warden finally said, "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ"‚Äîyou go home, the child will go with you. Sometimes he stayed with her sister (his Mausi) while she completed her training.

After B.Ed., her salary jumped to fifty rupees. "B.Ed. ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ B.Ed. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she explains pragmatically‚Äîthey were paying B.Ed. holders more, so she got the B.Ed. The practical value of education was clear to her, not just the theoretical knowledge but its concrete impact on life.

## **Following the Bank: A Nomadic Decade**

Her husband's career with Union Bank of India shaped their next decade. He progressed steadily‚Äîclerk to supervisor to special assistant to officer to manager‚Äîand with each promotion came transfers. "‡§á‡§∏‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ manager ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§è ‡§•‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ manager ‡§•‡•á," she notes‚Äîhe became a manager, a high position that brought bank housing wherever they went.

Jodhpur came first, from 1967 to 1973\. They lived in Shivniwas on Sardarpur B Road, a bank bungalow. "‡§¨‡§Ç‡§ó‡§≤‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ä," she confirms. Their first son was born there in February 1969, their second in 1973\. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ã‡§ß‡§™‡•Å‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡•à‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡•Å‡§è ‡§•‡•á," she says of the eldest. "‡§ö‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ã‡§ß‡§™‡•Å‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§è ‡§•‡•á ‡§¨‡§®‡•Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ," she adds of the second.

Those six years in Jodhpur meant "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã"‚Äîjust serving the children, raising them, managing the household. Her focus was complete: their development, their needs, their future.

Kota followed from 1973 to 1975\. "Shopping Center ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡•á ‡§•‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§´‡•ç‡§§‡§≤‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§® ‡§π‡•à ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ö‡•á ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§ä‡§™‡§∞ ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§® ‡§•‡§æ," she describes‚Äîthey lived above Muftlal's shop in the shopping center. Their third son was born there in 1974\. The house was walking distance from St. Paul's School where the boys studied.

Then Ajmer for less than a year in 1975-76. "‡§õ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•á," she estimates‚Äîsix months to a year. They lived near Raja Cycle and Martin Bridge in a bungalow with a courtyard, a Sanjina tree, and large airy rooms. "‡§¨‡§°‡§º‡§æ ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§•‡§æ ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ," she notes‚Äîit was a big house. But the stay was brief, another transfer already pending.

Udaipur claimed them from 1976 to 1981, a full five years. "‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡•á ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she confirms. They lived first on Residency Road, then moved to Bhatt Ji Ki Badi, both in the same general area near Bhopalpur. The lakes‚ÄîPichola, Swaroop Sagar, Fateh Sagar‚Äîlay just a few kilometers away. All three sons attended St. Paul's School in Bhopalpur.

Through all these moves, her purpose remained constant. "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§•‡§æ," she reflects‚Äîhow to advance ourselves, how to advance the children, this was always on her mind. The Economics education had shaped her thinking. She had studied how developed countries grew. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§•‡§æ ‡§¨‡§∏," she emphasizes‚Äîthis stayed in her mind.

## **The Jaipur Years Begin: Finding Home**

1981 brought them to Jaipur, and Jaipur would become home. "‡§ú‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞ 81 ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§è ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞," she states. They came when her eldest son was in seventh standard, the middle one in third, and the youngest in first. "‡§ú‡§¨ ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ï ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she declares‚Äîif the landlord doesn't want us, why should I stay?

Initially they lived behind Khasa Kothi, near the railway station and Gangaur Hotel. But the landlord wanted them out. The house belonged to someone named Lumba or Dumba, taken by the bank. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§æ ‡§≤‡•á‡§≤‡•ã," she insisted‚ÄîI won't live in such a house. Take another one. "‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¶‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§á‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§è," she explains. They paid to vacate the current residents from their chosen house and moved in.

That was 1981\. "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§§‡§ï ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä 42 ‡§á‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏ 42 ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç," she says. Forty-two years in the same house as of 2023\. "‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§ü‡•Ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§è ‡§•‡•á ‡§Ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•á ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§è‡§Ç‡§° ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§è ‡§•‡•á ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•á," she tries to recall‚ÄîSeptember-October or December, the end of the year 1981\. The exact month has blurred, but the fact remains: this became their permanent home.

## **The Choice: Career or Family**

Once settled in Jaipur, she made a conscious decision about her life's work. The principal of Seedling School, a higher secondary school, approached her: "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì"‚Äîcome teach at our school. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ü ‡§∏‡§ï‡§§‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§®‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§•‡•Ä," she responded‚ÄîI can't come, I had children at home.

Instead, she taught privately. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡•à‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§ü‡•á‡§¨‡§≤ ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§¨‡•à‡§† ‡§ï‡•á," she explains‚Äîshe taught in batches, sitting at the table at home. "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§π‡§æ‡§• ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§≤‡•á," she says with satisfaction. Children taught by her turned out very well. They passed their exams. "‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§§‡§ï ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she notes‚Äîtheir mothers still meet her today, grateful for the education their children received.

Her reasoning for not working outside was clear and practical. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§®‡•å‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡§§‡•á," she explains. If she took a job, she would have to do two works‚Äîthe job and household work. "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§è‡§ï ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§°‡§º ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§∏‡§∞ ‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã," she continues‚Äînow only one work needs doing: household work.

She accepted the trade-offs frankly. "‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç," she acknowledges‚Äîif development doesn't happen in other areas, no problem. "‡§π‡•â‡§¨‡•Ä‡§ú ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§à," she admits‚Äîhobbies couldn't all be fulfilled. "‡§ú‡•ã ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§≤ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§à," she says‚Äîwhat she struggled to achieve, she couldn't fully do. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§π‡•à ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä," she concludes‚Äîthis is all my fate.

But her choice was deliberate. She had a vision shaped by her Economics education. "‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•å‡§•‡•á ‡§™‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she explains her philosophy. Three children, fourth is husband, fifth is herself. "‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§π‡•à," she declares. Their work is my work. "‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§á‡§ú‡§º ‡§µ‡§∞‡§∂‡§ø‡§™ ‡§π‡•à," she emphasizes‚Äîthat work IS worship. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç," she continues‚Äîthese are all God's beings. Serving them is serving God.

Moreover, she wasn't just raising three sons. "‡§∂‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡§® ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she notes‚Äîfrom the beginning, she lived among her husband's siblings. After just one year alone setting up the house, "‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¨‡§π‡§®‡•á‡§Ç ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§è‡§ï ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¨‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§è," she explains‚Äîhis two sisters and one brother came to live with them. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ," she states‚Äîfive people's work became her responsibility.

"‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§Ü‡§ì‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§®‡•å‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§â‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she details‚Äîtheir weddings, their education, their jobs, she helped with all of it. "‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ," she insists‚Äînever refused saying I won't do this work. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§®‡•Ç‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á?" she asks rhetorically‚Äîif virtuous work is happening, why become party to sin by refusing? "‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§Ü ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she would say‚Äîdo it, brother, I'm coming to help.

Her own educational degrees remained, unused in the professional sense. "‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§°‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ," she acknowledges‚Äîdespite having all those degrees. But she has no regrets about choosing family service over career advancement.

## **A Lifetime of Learning: Never Stop Growing**

What makes her story remarkable isn't just what she accomplished early in life, but that she never stopped learning. Even while raising children and managing a household that often included extended family, she pursued course after course, skill after skill.

In 1978, while still in Udaipur, she took a food preservation course. "‡§ü‡•â‡§´‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä, ‡§ú‡•á‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä, ‡§ú‡•à‡§Æ ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ, ‡§ï‡•à‡§Ç‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä, ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•á‡§∏ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§ñ‡§æ," she lists‚Äîtoffees, jellies, jams, candies, squashes, and syrups, she learned them all.

The moment they arrived in Jaipur in 1981, she enrolled in a cookery and bakery course at Khasa Kothi. "Government of India ‡§ö‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§§‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she notes‚Äîthe Government of India ran it. "‡§è‡§ï ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§•‡§æ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§≤‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§ü ‡§°‡•á‡§ú‡§º ‡§™‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she explains‚Äîone month, alternate days. "‡§™‡§ø‡§ú‡§º‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡§æ ‡§π‡•à, ‡§ï‡•á‡§ï ‡§π‡•à," she adds‚Äîpizza, cakes, all bakery items.

In 1987, six years after settling in Jaipur, she took a six-month cutting and tailoring course. "‡§ï‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ü‡§®‡§æ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ü ‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡§ø‡§≤‡§®‡§æ ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã," she defines it‚Äîcutting cloth and sewing what you've cut. The course was comprehensive: "‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§≤‡§®‡§æ, ‡§¨‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§ø‡§≤‡§®‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§´‡•ç‡§∞‡•â‡§ï ‡§µ‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§π ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•á, ‡§¨‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§â‡§ú ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•á, ‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•á, ‡§®‡§æ‡§á‡§ü ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ü ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•á, ‡§™‡•á‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•á, ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä," she enumerates‚Äîunderwear, vests, frocks, blouses, salwar kameez, nightsuits, pants, children's shirts‚Äîeverything.

She joined the Kitchen Gardening Association on Tank Road. "‡§ï‡§à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§è ‡§â‡§∏‡§®‡•á," she says‚Äîwon several prizes for her gardening work. Her nephew now runs the small gardening center.

Around 1987, she and her husband both took astrology courses. "‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§≤‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§•-‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∑ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she explains‚Äîwhen your grandfather started learning, I also did the astrology course with him. The year is somewhat unclear in her memory‚Äî"‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§´‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§ü ‡§¶‡•á‡§ñ‡•Ç‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§è‡§ó‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡•à‡§ï‡•ç‡§ü ‡§à‡§Ø‡§∞ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ï‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she notes‚Äîif she looked at the certificates, she could give the exact year. But she later confirms it was 2001, in Chennai. "‡§ï‡§æ‡§´‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§è ‡§â‡§® ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã," she reflects‚Äîmany years have passed since then.

Her music education, begun in 1954 with tabla and harmonium, continued intermittently. She gave the second year exam from Allahabad University, bought the third year book, but stopped when her young brother-in-law died at forty-one. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§ï‡§π‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§≤‡§π‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§¨‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚Äîpeople would say she's playing music when her young brother-in-law has died. Social propriety in mourning demanded she stop. "‡§á‡§∏‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§¶ ‡§®‡•á ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she emphasizes‚ÄîI myself stopped, by my own choice.

Even first aid training came early, in 1959 in Delhi, from St. Ambulance. She later taught food preservation herself for a month at Maharaja School, passing on what she had learned to others.

Her daughter-in-law Kokila compiled all these certificates into one collection, making it easy to reference a lifetime of learning. Every few years, a new skill, a new qualification, a new capability. At age sixty-one, she completed the astrology course. This is a woman who never stopped growing, never stopped adding to her knowledge and abilities.

## **Teaching Values: The Three Core Principles**

Yet of all the education she received, the most fundamental came from her mother. "‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä," she explains‚Äîmy mother used to say, meaning their grandmother. Three principles, simple and clear:

"‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã"‚ÄîDon't steal. "‡§ù‡•Ç‡§† ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§¨‡•ã‡§≤‡•ã"‚ÄîDon't lie. "‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§≠ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì"‚ÄîDon't hurt anyone with your tongue.

"‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," her mother concluded‚Äîthis itself is serving God. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she states‚Äîand this same dharma I followed. These weren't abstract principles but practical guidelines lived every day.

She passed them to her children with equal firmness. Teaching them to share was lesson one. "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ç‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§æ‡§è ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§¶‡§ø‡§è," she illustrates‚Äîlike grapes, she would distribute to all three sons. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ ‡§¨‡•á‡§ü‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§•‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ä‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä," she would add‚Äîson, give me a couple too, I also want to eat. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚Äîso this entered the children's minds: we must share what we get. The rule was absolute: "‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ü ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì"‚Äîwhatever you eat, eat by sharing.

On honesty, she was equally unwavering. "‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she taught‚Äîdon't take anyone's thing by stealing. If they found something lying around: "‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á ‡§¶‡•ã"‚Äîgive it to the temple. If something of unclear provenance came to them: "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•ã ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§≤‡•ã"‚Äîdon't keep that thing, don't take it. The right way was clear: "‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§π‡§®‡§§ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã"‚Äîearn by your own hard work.

She enforced this strictly. "‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§™‡•á‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∏ ‡§¶‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ì," she recalls‚Äîeven if they took a pencil by mistake, I said return it immediately. "‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ä‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she would threaten‚Äîif you don't, I'll go to school and return it myself. The result: "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∏ ‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§•‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡•Ä"‚Äîthey never brought anything home belonging to others. They learned: you will not steal.

She taught by example too. Never hiring tutors, she taught all three sons herself through twelfth standard. "‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§∂‡§® ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ó‡§æ‡§à ‡§è‡§ï ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she states emphatically‚Äînever hired tuitions even once for them at our home. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§á‡§® ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã," she continues‚Äîand moreover, I myself taught all three children.

Her eldest, when he started giving tuitions himself in twelfth standard for IIT Chemistry preparation, had learned from her teaching. The values and the knowledge both passed from generation to generation through her dedication.

## **The Philosophy of the Four Ashrams**

As she reached her eighties, her understanding of life's structure became clearer and more important to her. "‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç," she explains‚Äîthere are four ashrams, four stages of life. She can recite them precisely:

"‡§è‡§ï ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"‚ÄîBal Ashram, childhood, from birth to twenty-five. "‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"‚ÄîGrihastha Ashram, householder stage, twenty-five to fifty. "‡§è‡§ï ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"‚ÄîVanprastha Ashram, retirement stage, fifty to seventy-five. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§è‡§ï ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ"‚ÄîAnd Sanyas Ashram, renunciation stage, seventy-five onward.

"‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§à," she declares‚Äînow I've entered the Sanyas Ashram at eighty-one. What this means shapes her entire current existence. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚ÄîI must leave worldly attachments. "‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á-‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§π‡§∞ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ó‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she continues‚Äîgradually cut off from everything and engage in God.

This isn't mere theory. It manifests in concrete changes. "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ù‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä," she notes‚Äîdon't like too much pomp and show now. "‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä," she adds‚Äîdon't like going to weddings. "‡§Ö‡§ï‡•á‡§≤‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she states‚Äîprefer to stay alone. "‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•à," she reasons‚Äîso I can focus on my daily routine.

"‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§§‡§∞‡§π ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ç," she summarizes her goal‚Äîwhatever ashram stage I'm passing through, I should pass through it properly. Looking back, she can evaluate her life by this framework.

"‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç," she reflects‚Äîin childhood stage, did childhood things properly. "‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç," she continues‚Äîin householder stage, did all household duties. "‡§¨‡§æ‡§™ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§º‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§ü‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ," she details‚Äîyour Papa's wedding and all responsibilities, everything completed. "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§™‡•à‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡•Å‡§è ‡§§‡•ã ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§°‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§â‡§§‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡§æ," she adds‚Äîlike when you all were born, celebrating birthdays, mundan ceremonies, all those things.

Now in Sanyas Ashram, her focus has shifted fundamentally. The time for social obligations has passed. The time for spiritual practice has arrived.

## **Daily Spiritual Practice: The Morning Routine**

Every morning at seven o'clock sharp, she walks to the temple. "7:00 ‡§¨‡§ú‡•á ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she states‚Äîthe aarti happens at seven. She attends not one but three aartis sequentially. "‡§è‡§ï ‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§∂‡§ø‡§µ ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•á 7:00 ‡§¨‡§ú‡•á," she lists‚Äîfirst is Shiv Ji's aarti. "‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§ì‡§Æ ‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∂ ‡§π‡§∞‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£ ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§ï‡•Ä," she continues‚Äîsecond is the Om Jai Jagdish Hare for Ram, Krishna, Laxman, Sita, Hanuman, and Radha Govind. "‡§§‡•Ä‡§∏‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§ó‡§£‡•á‡§∂ ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä," she completes‚Äîthird is Ganesh Ji's aarti.

"‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§≤‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she explains‚Äîafter all three aartis, taking prasad, then I return home. "‡§ï‡§≤ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ó‡§è ‡§•‡•á ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she notes during the interview‚Äîyesterday your Papa also went to the aarti. Gradually, the next generation begins joining her practices.

Returning home, she faces her second major spiritual practice: writing. "‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú‡§º ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she states‚ÄîI write two pages daily. Not just any writing‚Äîshe writes "‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ" repeatedly, methodically, devotionally.

Her system is precise. "‡§õ‡§π ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡§Æ ‡§¨‡§®‡•á ‡§π‡•Å‡§è ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç 37 ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç," she explains‚Äîsix columns per page, thirty-seven names per column. "‡§õ‡§π ‡§ï‡•â‡§≤‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç 222 ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç," she calculates‚Äî222 names total per page. Since 108 names equal one mala (rosary count), "16 ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she notes‚Äîtwo malas of 108 complete per page. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ," she concludes‚Äîso two pages equal four malas. "‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú‡§º ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ‡§®‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•à," she emphasizes‚Äîwriting this daily is my work.

She's already filled half a notebook. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ï‡•â‡§™‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§ú‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ," she shows during the video call, displaying pages of neat, repetitive writing. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§á‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ß‡§æ ‡§≠‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ï," she indicates‚Äîand in this I've filled half.

But her system includes an ingenious safeguard. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§™‡•á‡§ú ‡§è‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä," she explains‚ÄîI write two pages in advance. The reasoning came from bitter experience. "‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§π‡•â‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§ü‡§≤ ‡§ó‡§à ‡§•‡•Ä," she recalls‚ÄîI went to hospital on the third. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§•‡§æ," she notes with satisfaction‚Äîbut my third's writing was already done. When she returned on the fifth, she wrote for the fourth and fifth. "‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§è‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§è‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡§π‡•Å‡§Ç‡§ö ‡§ó‡§à ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•á," she continues‚Äîdoing like this, advancing day by day, now I've reached several days ahead.

"‡§î‡§∞ ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she reflects with deep feeling. From this writing, she has received very good peace. "‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•á," she emphasizes‚Äîthrough this writing, inner peace arrives.

Her third practice is reading. "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ç," she states simply‚ÄîI read Gita. The Bhagavad Gita gives her something essential. "‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§® ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚ÄîGita gives me knowledge of how to live life. "‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ù‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she continues‚Äîhow to understand others, what are these beings. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she asks‚Äîwhat is this nature. "‡§™‡•á‡§°‡§º ‡§™‡•å‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡§∂‡•Å ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä ‡§á‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§®‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§®‡•á ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á," she muses‚Äîtrees, plants, animals, birds, humans‚Äîwhy did God make all these, how were they made.

Recently she's been attending Shiv Puran discourses at the temple. "24 ‡§®‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§î‡§∞ 30 ‡§®‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§§‡§ï ‡§∏‡•Å‡§® ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•Ä," she notes‚Äîfrom November 24 to 30, she completed listening to one. Another series was scheduled from December 30 to January 9 during the interview. "‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§π‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ 30 ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ñ ‡§∏‡•á 9 ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ñ ‡§§‡§ï ‡§ö‡§≤‡•á‡§ó‡§æ," she explains‚Äîour temple will have Shiv Puran from the 30th to the 9th.

These discourses teach "‡§∏‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à"‚Äîwhat is creation and how should we live. But she's thoughtful about application. The texts describe Satya Yuga, Treta Yuga, Dwapara Yuga, and now Kaliyuga. "‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§´‡§ø‡§ü ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•à‡§†‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she observes astutely‚Äîthose old practices don't fit here now. Times have changed. "‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡§ø‡§® ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§§‡§ï ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§â‡§® ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§π‡•à ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§™‡§ï‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•ã," she advises‚Äîbut whatever is the essence, the purpose, the goal‚Äîhold onto THAT. "‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡•á ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ï‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§π‡§ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§¨ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§≤‡•ã," she continues‚Äîeven if you interpret according to Kaliyuga times. "‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡§ø‡§® ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•á ‡§™‡§π‡•Å‡§Å‡§ö‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she insists‚Äîbut we must reach the goal.

## **The Philosophy of Karma and Rebirth**

Her spiritual study has given her a clear framework for understanding action and consequence. "‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§è ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§ó‡•Ä," she explains‚ÄîGita says if you do satvik (pure) actions, you'll get divine birth. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§è ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§ó‡•Ä," she continues‚Äîif rajasic (passionate) actions, human birth. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§è ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§ü ‡§™‡§§‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Å ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§ó‡•Ä," she completes‚Äîif tamasic (dark) actions, you'll become insects, moths, lower life forms.

The law of return is precise. "‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á," she states‚Äîgive happiness, get happiness. "‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á," she continues‚Äîdo good for someone, give comfort, you'll receive it. "‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á," she warns‚Äîgive sorrow, get sorrow. "‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§≤‡§§ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•á," she elaborates‚Äîif you do wrong things.

But here's the crucial teaching: "‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç 10 ‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she emphasizes. After death, these things return tenfold. "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§è‡§ï ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§™‡§ï‡•ã ‚Çπ10 ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶," she illustrates‚Äîif you steal one rupee, you'll repay ten after death.

Why? Because of what accompanies you. "‡§Æ‡§® ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she explains‚Äîthe physical body doesn't go with you. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Ç‡§≤ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ," she states‚Äîthis gross body stays here. "‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ," she continues‚Äîthe subtle body goes. And with it: "‡§Æ‡§®, ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§, ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§á‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§Å‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ," she details‚Äîmind, consciousness, aspects, intellect, and the five actions of the senses. "‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡§æ," she gives example‚Äîhearing. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§á‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á," she concludes‚Äîall these sensory actions go with you. "‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§¨‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she adds‚Äîas Gita explains.

So her reasoning is clear: "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ã‡§ó ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§™‡§æ‡§è," she asks‚Äîwhy should we do deeds that lead to lower birth and suffering? "‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è," she answers‚Äîwe should do good deeds so we go to good rebirth. "‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§∏," she summarizes‚Äîkeep good thoughts, that's all.

Interestingly, she doesn't want moksha, liberation from the cycle entirely. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§¨‡•à‡§† ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è," she declares‚ÄîI don't want moksha where I go to God and just sit there. Instead: "‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì ‡§•‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§® ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§â‡§§‡§®‡•á ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∏ ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì," she explains‚Äîdo good deeds, go to God's realm, enjoy for a while according to your punya (merit), then come back. "‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•á‡§ó‡§æ," she continues‚Äîwill have to take birth again in the mortal world. She wants to keep serving, keep coming back, keep being useful. Permanent mergence with God doesn't appeal to her service-oriented nature.

## **Dealing with People: Making Friends, Not Enemies**

Her approach to human relationships reflects deep psychological understanding. "‡§¨‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§à ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•á‡§ñ ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§®‡•á ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó ‡§¶‡•ã," she advises‚Äîif you see evil in someone, leave it right there. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Å‡§π ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§°‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§ï‡§°‡§º ‡§≤‡•ã," she continues‚Äîturn your face and take your own path.

"‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§§‡§∞‡§π ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä," she observes‚Äîin this world you'll find all types. "‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á," she states‚Äîgood people and bad people both. The critical instruction: "‡§ò‡•É‡§£‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã"‚Äîdon't hate anyone. Why? "‡§ú‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§¨‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•á‡§Ç"‚Äîbecause it strikes back at you. Hatred returns to the hater.

"‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å ‡§™‡•à‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã," she commands‚Äîdon't create enemies. "‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§ì ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•ã," she instructs‚Äîmake everyone friends. She explains the fundamental choice we face with every person: "‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•à ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å ‡§π‡•à"‚Äîhuman being is their own friend, their own enemy.

"‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•á ‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§ö‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ," she illustrates the negative mindset‚Äîif you think of people as enemies, "Oh no, where did they come from?" But if you think positively: "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•á ‡§¨‡§°‡§º‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü"‚Äîa friend is meeting, how wonderful\! "‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§è‡§ï ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è‡§ó‡§æ," she notes‚Äîin your mind either confusion or clarity comes.

To remove this confusion: "‡§®‡§æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§®‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ì," she advises‚Äîneither be too happy nor sad. "‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã," she instructs‚Äîconsider everyone equal. "‡§ï‡§ø ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§™‡§ï‡§°‡§º ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡•ã," she guides‚Äîcatch the good things and move forward. "‡§â‡§®‡§ï‡•ã ‡§´‡•á‡§Ç‡§ï ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ï‡§ö‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ü‡•ã‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç," she concludes‚Äîthrow the bad things in the garbage basket.

When someone insults you, her mother's teaching applies. "‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§®‡•á ‡§ó‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§à ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ," her mother said‚Äîif someone gives you an insult, it's not yours if you don't accept it. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§® ‡§≤‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§•‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§á‡§∏‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ," she explains‚Äîwe didn't even pay attention to what they said.

"‡§™‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§§‡§¨ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she admits honestly‚Äîbut sometimes it hurt. When pain came, "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ ‡§π‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡§π‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡§§‡§æ ‡§•‡§æ," she explains‚Äîto lighten the sorrow, she had to tell someone. "‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§ú ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü," she would share‚Äîbrother, this happened today. "‡§¨‡§æ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§® ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§Ü," she notes‚Äîbut didn't seek solution or revenge. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§≤‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•á," she continues‚Äîjust kept moving forward with it.

Her action was measured: "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§â‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§°‡§º‡•á," she explains‚Äîdecided to stay away from that person so I hear minimum from them. "‡§™‡§∞ ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ú‡§µ‡§æ‡§¨ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she emphasizes‚Äîbut didn't give them a reply. Didn't retaliate. "‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç‡§ï‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§• ‡§è‡§°‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ã ‡§∏‡§ï‡§§‡§æ," she reasons‚Äîbecause they can't adjust with us. "‡§Ö‡§≤‡§ó ‡§∞‡§π‡•á ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á," she concludes‚Äîthey're different from our thoughts and values. Better to maintain distance than create ongoing conflict.

"‡§§‡•ã ‡§ê‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§º‡§ø‡§Ç‡§¶‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she summarizes‚Äîthis is how I led my life. No gossip‚Äî"‡§î‡§∞ ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§Æ‡•å‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ ‡§ó‡§™‡§∂‡§™ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç," she notes‚Äîwherever I got opportunity, I didn't gossip. Focus on work, avoid negativity, make friends, keep distance from those who can't be friends, but never create enemies.

"‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§® ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she reflects‚Äîmy life now is proceeding like this.

## **The Debt Philosophy: Serving Without Creating Obligation**

As she's grown older, a particular philosophy has intensified. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§•‡•Ä," she reflects‚ÄîI was indebted to everyone. "‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§á‡§®‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã," she explains‚Äîwhich I kept repaying like loans, serving them.

But now her thinking has evolved. "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§Ü ‡§ó‡§à," she notes‚Äînow this has come to my mind. "‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•Ä," she states‚Äîdon't take anyone's service. "‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡•á ‡§¨‡•á‡§ü‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ã," she continues‚Äîeven if it's your own son. "‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö‡§≤‡•ã," she instructs‚Äîdo his work yourself too. "‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ã‡§£ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ä‡§™‡§∞ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§¢‡§º‡•á," she reasons‚Äîso his debt doesn't accumulate on me.

"‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ã‡§£ ‡§ö‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚Äîone being becomes indebted to another being. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡§∞‡§æ‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ," she illustrates‚ÄîI did your work, you did mine, we're equal. "‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§º‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ä‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Ä," she warns‚Äîif you keep doing for me, I become indebted for the service.

"‡§á‡§∏‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she concludes‚Äîtherefore my mind has become like this. At eighty-one, she still does all her own cleaning, organizing, and housework. She can't compromise on three things: "‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§´‡§æ‡§à ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ ‡§â‡§†‡§æ‡§à ‡§á‡§®‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§§‡§ï ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ù‡•å‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§à," she states‚Äîhealth, cleanliness, and organizing, I haven't been able to compromise on these even till now.

"‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§π‡§æ‡§•‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¨‡§π ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¨‡§π ‡§∏‡§´‡§æ‡§à ‡§µ‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§π ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å," she emphasizes‚ÄîI do cleaning with my own hands every morning. This includes everything‚Äîdustbins scrubbed with soap if needed, buckets and mugs washed before every bath, fresh water from the tap only, never reusing water even if someone else bathed. "‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§• ‡§π‡§ú‡§º‡•Ä‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§® ‡§∞‡§ñ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å," she states‚Äîcomplete attention to hygiene.

The philosophy extends to teaching. "‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á-‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§Ü‡§™ ‡§∏‡•ã‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§â‡§† ‡§ï‡•á ‡§§‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã," she instructs‚Äîmake your own bed after getting up. "‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ò‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•ã," she continues‚Äîorganize everything in the house. This isn't just about cleanliness but about self-sufficiency, about not creating debts of service even within family.

## **The Health Crisis and Recovery**

January 2023 brought a moment that could have been fatal. "‡§§‡•Ä‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ñ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§π‡•â‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§ü‡§≤ ‡§ó‡§à ‡§•‡•Ä," she recounts‚ÄîI went to hospital on the third. Her blood sugar had dropped dangerously. "31 ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•á‡§µ‡§≤ ‡§™‡§π‡•Å‡§Å‡§ö ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ," she states‚Äîreached thirty-one. This is critically, life-threateningly low.

Her grandson Somya's reaction captured the family's terror: "‡§¶‡•ã‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•ã‡§®‡•á ‡§≤‡§ó ‡§ó‡§è," she remembers‚Äîboth started crying. "‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ? ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ?" she repeats‚ÄîSomya crying, "What happened to Dadi? What happened to Dadi?"

But Bhavya acted instantly. "‡§≠‡§µ‡•Ç ‡§á‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§è‡§ü‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡•á ‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ," she says‚ÄîBhavya immediately took me. "‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§Å‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§ü ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•á‡§∞ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ," she reflects soberly‚Äîif even five minutes delay had happened, who knows what would have happened. "‡§°‡•â‡§ï‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§®‡•á ‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ," she adds‚Äîas the doctor said. Those five minutes could have been the difference between life and death.

The doctor's orders changed her routine fundamentally. "‡§°‡•â‡§ï‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§π‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ã-‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ò‡§Ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì," she explains‚Äîdoctor said eat every two hours. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ã-‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ò‡§Ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§≤‡§ó ‡§ó‡§à," she states‚Äîso I started eating every two hours. "‡§≠‡§æ‡§à ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡•ã ‡§™‡§π‡§≤‡•á ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ó‡•ã," she instructs herself‚Äîbrother, leave work, first focus on eating. "‡§ï‡•Å‡§õ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§≤ ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§™‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã," she continues‚Äîeat anything, drink coconut water, then work.

"‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º‡•á‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶ ‡§π‡•à," she notes‚Äîthese are the things I like now. Priority has shifted from work to health maintenance. "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•Å‡§Ü‡§è‡§Å ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§à," she says with gratitude‚Äînow all of you people's prayers worked. "‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she concludes simply‚ÄîI'm living.

## **The Steel Body at Eighty-One**

Looking back at her physical journey, the progression is remarkable. The childhood of walking, carrying water, playing sports, doing drill, practicing throwball (baseball), the NCC training with actual rifle firing, the march practices, the coordination with musical sticks‚Äîall of it built what she proudly calls her steel body.

"‡§ú‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•à‡§Ç‡§° ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•Ä‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•â‡§°‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ‡§à ‡§¨‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she recalls telling her in-laws. They built and gave her a body of steel. "‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§™‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§õ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç," she declares‚Äîany amount of work, no illness comes.

The only exception: "‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§á‡§ü‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•Ä ‡§•‡•Ä," she notes‚Äîonly from cold, bronchitis would come. This happened during the hectic years of raising children, constantly going in and out, temperature changes. "‡§§‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§á‡§ü‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§à," she explains‚Äîthen bronchitis came in my life. "‡§¨‡§æ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§à," she emphasizes‚Äîotherwise no other illness came.

At eighty-one, medical professionals confirm the results of that steel body. Her teeth, strengthened by decades of sugarcane chewing: "‡§ú‡§ø‡§∏ ‡§°‡•â‡§ï‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞ ‡§®‡•á ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§á‡§≤‡§æ‡§ú ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ 81 80 ‡§á‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§ì‡§≤‡•ç‡§° ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§â‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ã ‡§â‡§∏‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§™‡§ï‡•á ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§ú‡§º‡§¨‡•Ç‡§§ ‡§π‡•à," she reports‚Äîthe doctor who recently treated me at eighty-eighty-one said your teeth are very strong.

Her eyes, maintained by that childhood sadhu's teaching: "‡§â‡§∏‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§Ç‡§ñ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤ ‡§†‡•Ä‡§ï ‡§π‡•à," she states‚Äîfrom this my eyes are completely fine. "‡§Æ‡§§‡§≤‡§¨ ‡§®‡§∏‡•á‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§π ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§´‡•Ä ‡§†‡•Ä‡§ï ‡§π‡•à ‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§® ‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ," she adds‚Äîmy nerves etc. are very good as the surgeon explained. "‡§¶‡§ø‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å ‡§Ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§™‡•á ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§â‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ä 81 ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§â‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•à," she continues‚ÄîI keep showing my eyes regularly even at this age of eighty-one. "‡§§‡•ã ‡§â‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§†‡•Ä‡§ï ‡§π‡•à ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä," she concludes‚Äîthey were good then, they're good now.

Recent health scare aside, the foundation built in childhood continues supporting her eighth decade.

## **The Video Call: Connecting Generations**

The interview itself, conducted via video call during winter break in January 2023, reveals the bridge between generations. Her grandchildren, calling from abroad, show her their virtual reality experiences‚Äî"‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡•Å‡§Ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§≤‡§ø‡§ü‡•Ä," a new technology she's never heard of. They explain the digital world you can see through devices. "‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ," she responds with interest‚ÄîI see.

They share their artwork. Naman shows his burn art on wood, resin art pieces, calligraphy and lettering practice. "‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∏‡•á‡§ú ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§™‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è," he explains‚ÄîI wrote this message for you. "Enjoy Every Moment," the artwork reads. "‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ," she responds warmly‚Äîvery good.

They discuss their college studies‚Äîcomputer science, data science, entrepreneurship courses. "‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§," she approves‚Äîvery good thing. "‡§∏‡§´‡§≤‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡•á ‡§π‡•ã," she encourages‚Äîwalking on the path of success. "‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§π‡•à ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§¨‡§æ‡§§," she notes‚Äîdeveloping skills, good thing. "‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§π‡•â‡§¨‡•Ä ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•ã," she advises‚Äîkeep developing some hobby or other.

They show her Google Maps, searching for her old addresses. Dariba Kalan in Old Delhi‚Äî"‡§Ø‡§π ‡§π‡•à ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§π‡•à ‡§¶‡§∞‡•Ä‡§¨‡§æ ‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§® ‡§∞‡•ã‡§°," they point out. The railway bungalow locations, long changed. Ramjas College, still standing‚Äî"‡§Ø‡§π ‡§π‡•à ‡§Ü‡§™‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤," they confirm‚Äîthis is your school. She peers at the screen, memory and present converging. "‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§•‡§æ," she confirms‚Äîyes, it was like this.

St. Paul's School in Kota, Udaipur addresses, Jodhpur locations‚Äîone by one they reconstruct her geographic journey through technology. When her memory wavers on exact locations, "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•á‡§ü‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§á‡§§‡§®‡§æ," she admits‚Äîdon't remember now, son, that much. But when an image clicks: "‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§π‡•à ‡§á‡§ß‡§∞ ‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§°," she confirms‚Äîyes this is it, here she stayed.

It's 1:00 PM. "‡§ó‡•Å‡§° ‡§Ü‡§´‡•ç‡§ü‡§∞‡§®‡•Ç‡§® 1 ‡§ì ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•â‡§ï," someone notes‚Äîgood afternoon, one o'clock. "‡§π‡§æ‡§Å 1 PM ‡§π‡•à ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§™ ‡§≤‡§Ç‡§ö ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§ì ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä," they tell her‚Äîit's 1 PM, you eat lunch now. "‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§®‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ä‡§Å‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã," she responds‚ÄîI'll go meet someone now. Multiple "‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§Ø"s echo as the call ends, a conversation across continents, across generations, documenting a life that spanned from pre-Independence India to the digital age.

## **The Legacy: What Remains**

As the interview closes, what emerges isn't just a life story but a philosophy, a template for how to live with purpose, dignity, and constant growth.

From childhood she learned self-sufficiency‚Äîcarrying water when needed, walking to school regardless of distance, building physical strength through practical activity. She learned spiritual practices young and maintained them for eight decades. The eye-washing with water-filled mouth, the sugarcane chewing, the physical discipline‚Äîthese weren't temporary enthusiasms but lifetime commitments.

When education was denied her as a girl, she fought for it. Not with anger but with firm insistence: "‡§π‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§¢‡§º‡•á‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á"‚ÄîI will study. She struggled, especially for college, but never wavered. Her father eventually supported her, and she completed not just BA but MA, not to mention B.Ed. and decades of additional courses.

When Economics education showed her global development patterns, she applied them at home. India was developing, she would help develop her household. "‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§ó‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§¨‡§¢‡§º‡§æ‡§è‡§Ç," she made her mission‚Äîhow to advance ourselves, advance our children.

When faced with the choice between career and family, she chose deliberately. Two works or one? She chose one‚Äîhousehold work‚Äîbut elevated it to worship. "‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï ‡§á‡§ú‡§º ‡§µ‡§∞‡§∂‡§ø‡§™ ‡§π‡•à," she explained. Their work is my work, that work is worship. "‡§Ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§¨ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç," she reasoned‚Äîthese are all God's beings. Serving them was serving God.

She taught her children three core values from her mother: don't steal, don't lie, don't hurt with words. "‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," her mother had said‚Äîthis itself is serving God. She added lessons on sharing, on earning through own effort, on returning even borrowed pencils. The enforcement was firm. The results showed in three successful sons who learned honesty and hard work.

She never stopped learning. Even while raising three sons and often extended family, she pursued courses: food preservation in 1978, cookery and bakery in 1981, cutting and tailoring in 1987, kitchen gardening with prizes, music through second year, astrology in 2001, first aid in 1959\. Her daughter-in-law compiled the certificates‚Äîtestimony to six decades of continuous growth.

From the Gita and Puranas she extracted philosophical framework. The four ashrams gave her life structure. The karma philosophy guided her actions. "‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•á," she understood‚Äîgive happiness, get happiness. After death, tenfold return. So choose good actions, good thoughts.

Human relationships followed clear principles: make friends not enemies, throw bad things in garbage basket, don't hate because it returns to you, maintain distance from those incompatible but never create active conflict. "‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•à ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å ‡§π‡•à," she taught‚Äîhumans are their own friends, their own enemies. The choice is ours.

Even debt became spiritual concept. "‡§ï‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•Ä," she now believes‚Äîdon't take anyone's service. Even from own children. Do everything yourself so debt doesn't accumulate. "‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ã‡§£ ‡§ö‡§¢‡§º‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚Äîone being becomes indebted to another. At eighty-one, she still does all her own cleaning, maintaining standards that won't compromise.

The daily spiritual practice at eighty-one shows her current focus: three aartis at 7 AM, writing "Jai Shri Krishna" two pages daily (four malas), reading Gita, attending Puran discourses. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she testifies‚Äîfrom this I've received very good peace. The Sanyas Ashram stage means gradual detachment from world, increasing engagement with God. "‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§õ‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she explains‚ÄîI must leave worldly attachments. "‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á-‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à ‡§π‡§∞ ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§ú‡§º ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ó‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she continues‚Äîgradually cut from everything and engage in God.

Yet she doesn't want moksha, permanent mergence. "‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§¨‡•à‡§† ‡§ú‡§æ‡§è," she declares. She wants to keep returning, keep serving. "‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Å ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì ‡§•‡•ã‡§°‡§º‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§® ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§â‡§§‡§®‡•á ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§´‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∏ ‡§Ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ì," she explains‚Äîdo good, go to God, enjoy fruits of merit, then come back. The cycle continues because service continues.

When medical emergency struck‚Äîsugar level at thirty-one‚ÄîBhavya's immediate action saved her. "‡§Ö‡§ó‡§∞ ‡§™‡§æ‡§Å‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§ü ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•á‡§∞ ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ," she acknowledges‚Äîfive minutes could have been fatal. But prayers worked. "‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•Å‡§Ü‡§è‡§Å ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§à ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she says gratefully‚Äîeveryone's prayers worked, I'm living.

The steel body built in childhood, strengthened through decades of discipline, maintains her still. Eyes excellent from childhood water practice. Teeth strong from sugarcane. Overall health robust despite eighty-one years, one hospitalization, one chronic bronchitis from cold. She attributes everything to early foundation: physical training, wholesome food, disciplined practice, no compromises on cleanliness.

Her advice to grandchildren combines traditional and modern understanding. Keep developing skills. Keep learning. Make friends. Do good actions because they return tenfold. Serve but don't create debts. "‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§à ‡§π‡•â‡§¨‡•Ä ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§™ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•ã," she encourages‚Äîkeep developing hobbies. Growth doesn't stop at any age.

## **Conclusion: "Do or Die"**

If one phrase captures her life, it's the lesson from NCC that still runs in her mind after sixty years: "‡§°‡•Ç ‡§è‡§Ç‡§° ‡§°‡§æ‡§à"‚ÄîDo or Die. When girls weren't encouraged in education, she insisted and succeeded. When Economics was her weakest subject, she completed Honours. When career conflicted with family, she chose family but elevated it to spiritual practice. When courses were available, she took them into her sixties. When spiritual practice called, she answered with daily discipline. When health crisis struck, she recovered and adapted.

"‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§¨ ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§® ‡§π‡•à ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ê‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö‡§≤ ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à," she reflects at the interview's end‚Äîmy life now is proceeding like this. Not with complaint, not with regret, but with continued purpose. The four ashrams gave structure. The three principles from mother gave foundation. The karma philosophy gave motivation. The steel body gave capability. The continuous learning gave adaptability. The spiritual practice gave peace.

"‡§¨‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§π‡•Ä ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§§‡§∞‡§π ‡§ó‡•Å‡§ú‡§º‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ç," she summarizes‚Äîmy goal is whatever ashram stage I'm passing through, I pass through it properly. She did childhood properly. She did householder stage properly, raising family with values. She did retirement stage properly, managing ceremonies and celebrations. Now she does renunciation stage properly, focusing on God while maintaining dignity and independence.

"‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ñ‡•á‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§∏," she advises finally‚Äîkeep good thoughts, that's all. Simple advice from eight decades of living. Good thoughts, good actions, good karma. Serve without creating debt. Learn without stopping. Make friends without making enemies. Throw bad in garbage, keep good close. Share what you have. Return what you borrowed. Don't steal, don't lie, don't hurt with words‚Äîthis is serving God.

From pre-Independence railway bungalow with lamp-lit nights and carried water to video calls with grandchildren across continents discussing virtual reality, from walking miles to school with cloth bags to managing households across cities with three sons educated to success, from fighting for her own education to teaching generations without hired tutors, from learning dozens of courses to writing four malas of "Jai Shri Krishna" daily in neat columns‚Äîthis is a life lived with intention, adaptation, and unwavering commitment to growth and service.

At eighty-one, after recent brush with death, she continues. Three aartis each morning. Two pages of writing. Gita reading. Standards that don't compromise. "‡§î‡§∞ ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ù‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à," she testifies‚Äîfrom this I've received very good peace.

The grandchildren will return to their studies, their computer science and data science and entrepreneurship courses. The video call will end. But the documentation remains‚Äîa life that spanned nearly a century of change, maintained steel-body strength and clear-minded philosophy, fought necessary battles and avoided unnecessary ones, learned continuously and taught generously, chose service over career but elevated service to worship, and at eighty-one still writes daily prayers in neat columns, attends three aartis each morning, and maintains standards of cleanliness that won't compromise.

"Do or Die" she learned at nineteen. At eighty-one, she still lives it.

**Jai Shri Krishna.** üôè

---

*Compiled from video interview conducted January 2023, winter break, with grandchildren across continents. A life documented, a philosophy preserved, a legacy continued.*

# **Dadi Life Timeline**

# **Dadi's Life Timeline**

## **Early Years (1944-1956)**

**\~1944-1945** \- Birth

* Born in Delhi as the 7th child  
* Family: 4 brothers, 3 sisters  
* Father: Shri Ram Bhargava (Railway Mail Guard, born 1901\)  
* Mother: Narayani  
* Lived in railway quarters, large bungalow with servants' quarters

**1946-1950** \- Childhood

* Lived in various railway stations due to father's job  
* No running water or electricity initially  
* Water carried in aluminum cans (16 liters each)  
* Used oil lamps (lanterns) before electricity

**1950-1955** \- Elementary Education

* Attended Railway School, \~1.5 km walking distance  
* Got free milk at school (Railway benefit)  
* Daily routine: walking to school with cloth bag  
* Learned eye care exercises (still practices at 81\)  
* Ate sugarcane for strong teeth

**1954** \- Family Wedding

* Second eldest brother married in Gangapur City, Rajasthan

**1955** \- Father's Retirement

* Father retired from Railways  
* Received PF (Provident Fund), no pension

## **Education & Youth (1956-1967)**

**1956** (Age 16\) \- Move to Delhi

* Father retired, family moved to Delhi permanently  
* Address: 152 Katra Mashroom, Dariba Kalan, Old Delhi  
* Near Red Fort, Chandni Chowk, Splendor Road

**1956-1961** \- Secondary Education

* Government Higher Secondary School, Dariyaganj  
* Near Gandhi's memorial (Rajghat)  
* Walked 4-5 km daily (30 minutes)  
* Initially tried bus (‚Çπ1/month) but it stopped after one month  
* Studied through 9th, 10th, 11th grades

**1961-1964** \- College Years (Ramjas College)

* **Ramjas College, Morris Nagar, Delhi**  
* BA Honours in Economics  
* Traveled by special bus from Lal Kila to college  
* Member of Delhi School of Economics library  
* Read English writers: Bentham, Malthus  
* Only 4 girls in class of 22 students

**1962-1964** \- NCC Training

* **National Cadet Corps** (3 years: 1st, 2nd, 3rd year)  
* 1962: China-India War  
* 1963: **Rifle Training** received after war  
* Learned to march, handle rifles  
* Group leader for students  
* Philosophy: "Do and Die"

**Sports & Activities:**

* Throw ball (baseball-like game)  
* Lathi (stick) handling  
* Long jump  
* Malkhamb (pole gymnastics) \- group leader

**1960** \- Spiritual Practice

* Wrote 2,500 Gayatri Mantras  
* Sent to Mathura Tapobhumi  
* Read Krishna Leela and Ramayana to grandmother

**1954-1968** \- Music Training

* Learned Tabla and Harmonium  
* Passed 2nd year exam from Allahabad/Prayag University (Ilahabad)  
* Continued after marriage

**1964** \- Graduation

* Completed BA Honours Economics  
* Had distinction marks in Lower Mathematics and Domestic Science  
* 60% in Economics (lowest marks)

## **Marriage & Family Years (1967-1981)**

**1967** (Age \~23) \- Marriage

* Late marriage due to struggle for higher education  
* Husband: Union Bank of India employee

**1968** \- Higher Education Continues

* MA First Year from Meerut University  
* Transferred to Agra University for MA Final

**1968** (July-December) \- First Teaching Job

* Taught Mathematics (Arithmetic, Geometry, Algebra)  
* 8th class students  
* Salary: ‚Çπ15/month (before B.Ed)

**1969** (February) \- First Son Born

* Father of the interviewer born in **Jodhpur**

**1970-1971** \- B.Ed Completion

* Bachelor of Education degree  
* Did while raising first child  
* Stayed in hostel during course  
* Son insisted on coming with her once

### **Life in Jodhpur (1967-1973)**

**Location:** Sardarpura, B Road, Shivnivas

* 6 years total  
* Second son (Banu/Banoo) born here  
* Started teaching after B.Ed  
* Salary increased to ‚Çπ50/month after B.Ed  
* Taught at **Lalwani School**

### **Life in Kota (1973-1975)**

**Location:** Shopping Center, Gummanpura

* Above Mafatlal's shop  
* 2 years  
* Third son (Bhayu/Bhanu chacha) born in **1974**  
* Children attended **St. Paul's School**

### **Life in Ajmer (1975-1976)**

**Location:** Near Raja Cycle, Martingale Bridge

* Very short stay (6 months \- 1 year)  
* Large bungalow provided by bank  
* Children continued at **St. Anselm School**

### **Life in Udaipur (1976-1981)**

**Location:** Residency Road, later Bhatt ji ki Badi

* 5 years  
* Near Pichola, Swaroop Sagar, Fateh Sagar lakes  
* **1978: Food Preservation Course** \- learned to make toffee, jelly, jam, candy, squashes, syrups  
* Children attended **St. Paul's School, Sardarpura/Bhopal Pura**  
* Gave private tuitions at home

## **Jaipur Years (1981-Present)**

**1981** (September/October/December) \- Move to Jaipur

* First: Near Khasa Kothi (behind), near Railway Station  
* Near Ganggaur Hotel, Circuit House, Sanjay Gandhi Road  
* Temporary accommodation

**1981** (Late) \- **Permanent Home**

* Moved to current house (still living here after 42 years)  
* Sons' ages: 7th grade, 3rd grade, 1st grade

### **Courses & Skills Development**

**1981** \- **Cookery & Bakery Course**

* Government of India program at Khasa Kothi  
* One month course, alternate day classes  
* Learned pizza, cakes, baking

**1987** \- **Cutting & Tailoring Course**

* 6 months program  
* Learned to make jangias, vests, frocks, blouses, salwar kameez, night suits, pants, shirts

**1987\~** \- **Music Second Year**

* Continued harmonium training  
* Goyal teacher offered to help with exams  
* Stopped after husband's younger brother passed away at 41

**Late 1980s** \- **Astrology Course**

* Studied with husband  
* Both completed course

**2001** \- **Astrology Course** (Advanced)

* From Chennai

**Various** \- **Kitchen Garden Association**

* Joined and learned gardening  
* Won several prizes  
* Located on Tank Road

**1959** \- **First Aid Course** (Delhi)

* From St. Ambulance

### **Teaching in Jaipur**

* Gave private tuitions at home  
* Taught table sitting students  
* Known for teaching without looking at books  
* Excellent at mathematics  
* Students performed very well

## **Health & Spiritual Life**

**Recent** (2026) \- **Health Event**

* Hospitalized briefly  
* Sugar level dropped to 31  
* Recovered thanks to Bhayu chacha's quick action

**Current Daily Routine (Age 81):**

**Morning:**

* Wakes up early  
* Cleans house thoroughly (including dustbins with scrubber)  
* Everything must be spotlessly clean  
* Takes bath with fresh water from tap (empties bucket first)

**7:00 AM \- Temple Visit:**

1. Shiv ji aarti  
2. Om Jai Jagdish Hare (Ram, Krishna, Lakshman, Sita, Hanuman)  
3. Radha Govind aarti  
4. Ganesh ji aarti  
* Returns home after taking prasad

**Daily Spiritual Practice:**

* Writes "**Jai Shri Krishna**" in notebook  
* 2 pages daily \= 4 malas (rosaries)  
* 222 names per page (37 names √ó 6 columns)  
* 4 malas \= 432 repetitions daily  
* Keeps one day advance copy in case unable to write  
* Reads **Bhagavad Gita** daily for wisdom

**Recent Spiritual Events:**

* Attended Shiv Purana discourse (Nov 24-30, Dec 30\)  
* Studies four Ashramas (stages of life)  
* Currently in Sannyasa Ashram (75+)  
* Focus on detachment, spirituality, no worldly attachments

## **Life Philosophy & Values**

**Core Beliefs:**

* Education is essential for development  
* Self-reliance and hard work  
* No stealing \- "never take what isn't yours"  
* Share food \- "divide and eat together"  
* No lying, no hurting others' feelings  
* Service to family is worship of God  
* Three types of karma lead to three types of rebirth:  
  * Satvik karma ‚Üí Deva yoni (godly)  
  * Rajasik karma ‚Üí Manushya yoni (human)  
  * Tamasik karma ‚Üí Lower life forms  
* "Give happiness, receive happiness; give sorrow, receive sorrow"  
* Don't create enemies, make friends  
* See good in people, discard bad  
* No hatred for anyone

**Parenting Philosophy:**

* Taught all three sons herself until 12th grade  
* No tuitions for children  
* Focus on character building  
* Share everything equally  
* Never steal  
* Work hard honestly  
* Served extended family members  
* Never refused to help with family duties

## **Family Tree Summary**

**Her Parents' Generation:**

* Father: Shri Ram Bhargava (b. 1901, Railway Mail Guard)  
* Mother: Narayani (from Narnaul)  
* Grandfather: Hardayal Singh (from Rewari)  
* 8 children total (she was 7th)

**Her Generation:**

* 4 brothers, 3 sisters (2 older sisters, 1 younger sister)

**Her Family:**

* Husband: Union Bank of India Manager
